###begin article-title 0
A Network of Multi-Tasking Proteins at the DNA Replication Fork Preserves Genome Stability 
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 127 132 127 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2,</italic>
###xml 295 299 295 299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 416 420 416 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 694 699 694 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2,</italic>
###xml 212 217 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
To elucidate the network that maintains high fidelity genome replication, we have introduced two conditional mutant alleles of DNA2, an essential DNA replication gene, into each of the approximately 4,700 viable yeast deletion mutants and determined the fitness of the double mutants. Fifty-six DNA2-interacting genes were identified. Clustering analysis of genomic synthetic lethality profiles of each of 43 of the DNA2-interacting genes defines a network (consisting of 322 genes and 876 interactions) whose topology provides clues as to how replication proteins coordinate regulation and repair to protect genome integrity. The results also shed new light on the functions of the query gene DNA2, which, despite many years of study, remain controversial, especially its proposed role in Okazaki fragment processing and the nature of its in vivo substrates. Because of the multifunctional nature of virtually all proteins at the replication fork, the meaning of any single genetic interaction is inherently ambiguous. The multiplexing nature of the current studies, however, combined with follow-up supporting experiments, reveals most if not all of the unique pathways requiring Dna2p. These include not only Okazaki fragment processing and DNA repair but also chromatin dynamics.
###end p 1
###begin title 2
Synopsis
###end title 2
###begin p 3
###xml 358 363 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 672 677 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 874 879 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Maintenance of genome stability from generation to generation is a primary defense against mutation and ensuing disease. Thus, the cell has evolved complex mechanisms, consisting of redundant, partially overlapping pathways, to protect the fidelity of genome inheritance. Using modern genetic screening techniques that allow one to investigate every gene in yeast that might be involved in these pathways, the researchers have defined a network consisting of 322 genes that together safeguard the DNA replication process. Previous approaches were limited to defining the interaction of one or a few genes, but the availability of mutants affecting all of the nonessential yeast genes allowed the identification of over 800 interactions in this study. In addition, the synthetic genetic array technique used in this study allowed identification of every nonessential gene in yeast that interacts with an essential replication protein, Dna2p. The comprehensiveness of the approach identified most, if not all, of the pathways in which the multitasking Dna2p participates, in a single experiment. The genomic scale of the study significantly accelerates understanding of this protein over traditional, low-throughput genetic methods.
###end p 3
###begin title 4
Introduction
###end title 4
###begin p 5
In order to preserve the fidelity of genome duplication during DNA replication, cells with complex genomes have evolved a network of pathways composed of the DNA replication apparatus, DNA repair proteins, and regulatory activities. Despite years of general characterization, knowledge of the specific mechanisms by which these pathways are integrated to protect the genome is still incomplete because of the complexity of underlying replication fork processes and their regulation. The challenge in understanding high fidelity genome transmission has progressed from identification and characterization of the individual DNA replication components to investigation of how they combine to form pathways orchestrating repair and regulation.
###end p 5
###begin p 6
###xml 401 407 401 407 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 536 537 536 537 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b001">1</xref>
###xml 540 546 540 546 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 662 663 662 663 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b002">2</xref>
###xml 735 736 735 736 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b003">3</xref>
###xml 737 738 737 738 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b004">4</xref>
###xml 1290 1291 1286 1287 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b005">5</xref>
###xml 1292 1293 1288 1289 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b006">6</xref>
###xml 1326 1350 1322 1346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 1362 1368 1358 1364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD27,</italic>
###xml 1430 1436 1426 1432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1466 1478 1462 1474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 rad27</italic>
###xml 1523 1524 1515 1516 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b007">7</xref>
###xml 1525 1526 1517 1518 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b008">8</xref>
###xml 1802 1803 1790 1791 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b009">9</xref>
###xml 1804 1806 1792 1794 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b013">13</xref>
###xml 2003 2005 1991 1993 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b012">12</xref>
###xml 2782 2784 2766 2768 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b014">14</xref>
###xml 448 453 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 1256 1260 <span type="species:ncbi:10633?0.9966199903428296">SV40</span>
###xml 1326 1350 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
The first line of defense against genome instability resides with the enzymes of the DNA replication apparatus itself. While the most familiar example is the proofreading activity found in the DNA polymerases, other proteins of the replisome have also evolved substrate specificities to address errors made during replication fork progression. One of these proteins is Dna2p, a helicase/nuclease. The dna2-1 mutation was identified in a screen for yeast mutants defective in DNA replication based on an assay using permeabilized cells [1]. dna2-1 strains were then shown to accumulate subgenomic-size DNA fragments when incubated at the restrictive temperature [2]. Dna2p has both DNA helicase and single-stranded nuclease activities [3,4]. Biochemical and genetic characterization has revealed that Dna2p is involved in the processing of some, but not all, Okazaki fragments. Specifically, it has been proposed that Dna2p acts with FEN1 to remove RNA primers from Okazaki fragments whose 5' RNA/DNA termini have been extensively displaced by DNA polymerase (pol) delta. Four lines of evidence support a role for Dna2p in Okazaki fragment processing (OFP). First, Dna2p co-purifies with FEN1, which is a structure-specific nuclease required for OFP in the SV40 in vitro replication system [5,6]. Second, overexpression of the Saccharomyces cerevisiae FEN1 gene, RAD27, suppresses the temperature-sensitive (ts) growth defect of a dna2-1 strain, and furthermore, the dna2-1 rad27Delta double mutant is synthetically lethal [7,8]. Third, biochemical reconstitution experiments have shown that excessive strand displacement by pol delta creates long 5' flaps that are cleaved inefficiently by FEN1, and that initial cleavage of these flaps by Dna2p potentiates more efficient subsequent cleavage by FEN1 [9-13]. Finally, Dna2p prefers to act on flaps with secondary structures in vitro, i.e., hairpins or fold-backs containing CTG repeats, which is probably where helicase functionality becomes necessary [12]. Thus, the Dna2p nuclease has evolved the ideal mechanism for highly specific action at a replication fork, requiring the presence of an unpaired 5' terminus for activity, and displaying a complete lack of activity for single-stranded gaps in duplex DNA, which would result in recombinogenic double-strand breaks (DSBs). Nevertheless, there is a real question of whether the excessively displaced flaps used to study Dna2p in vitro ever occur in vivo, and some biochemical evidence suggests this may not be the case. Therefore, although biochemical data indicate that Dna2p is required for OFP when FEN1 or pol delta activity is impaired, identification of Dna2p's in vivo substrates requires more appropriate genetic and physiological assays than have been applied to date [14].
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 324 326 324 326 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b015">15</xref>
###xml 516 520 516 520 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 619 620 619 620 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b008">8</xref>
###xml 621 623 621 623 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b016">16</xref>
###xml 624 626 624 626 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b017">17</xref>
The second and third lines of defense for preventing genome instability during DNA replication are the DNA repair pathways and regulatory pathways, such as cell cycle checkpoints. Increasing evidence suggests that these pathways are integrated into the replication pathway through their use of certain replication proteins [15]. Dna2p seems to be one of these multitasking proteins. Besides its function in OFP, our evidence strongly suggests that Dna2p provides a link between DNA replication and DNA repair, since dna2 mutants are sensitive to methyl methane sulfonate (MMS), X-rays, bleomycin, and hydroxyurea (HU) [8,16,17].
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 219 223 219 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 236 238 236 238 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b018">18</xref>
###xml 239 241 239 241 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b019">19</xref>
To provide a comprehensive view of the roles of Dna2p at the replication fork and in other genome maintenance pathways, we conducted a large-scale synthetic lethal screen by synthetic genetic array (SGA) analysis using DNA2 as a query [18,19]. Two genes are synthetically lethal if single mutants, defective in either gene, are viable, while double mutants, defective in both genes, are inviable. Two mutants are synthetically sick if the double mutant grows significantly slower than either single mutant. Synthetic lethality is useful for identifying redundancy and complementarity, e.g., pathways that compensate for functional deficiencies in each other or genes encoding products that are both required to efficiently process a common substrate, which is often the case for DNA replication and repair proteins. Synthetic lethal screens not only reveal previously unknown genetic interactions with queried mutants but also how gene products and their corresponding pathways functionally associate.
###end p 8
###begin p 9
Our results provide a catalogue of most, if not all, pathways that are interdependent with or require Dna2p, thus revealing both the extent and limits of its multitasking character. The work not only confirms a role in OFP, but also identifies functions in (1) a replication/repair helicase subnet, (2) DSB repair and mismatch repair, (3) the replication stress checkpoint, (4) sister chromatid cohesion, (5) chromatin dynamics, (6) histone modification, and (7) osmotic and oxidative stress responses. In a more general sense, the interactions link a specific network of DNA repair and regulatory pathways to a specific network of replication genes that together maintain high fidelity lagging-strand DNA replication.
###end p 9
###begin title 10
Results
###end title 10
###begin title 11
SGA Screens
###end title 11
###begin p 12
###xml 6 10 6 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 141 148 141 148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1,</italic>
###xml 212 219 212 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2,</italic>
###xml 320 321 308 309 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b008">8</xref>
###xml 322 324 310 312 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b020">20</xref>
###xml 327 333 315 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 445 446 433 434 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b003">3</xref>
###xml 615 617 603 605 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b021">21</xref>
###xml 624 630 612 618 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 733 734 721 722 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b008">8</xref>
###xml 760 763 748 751 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PCR</italic>
###xml 836 838 824 826 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b022">22</xref>
###xml 845 851 833 839 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1004 1010 992 998 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1040 1046 1028 1034 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1155 1161 1143 1149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1187 1191 1175 1179 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
Since DNA2 is an essential gene, either a conditional or hypomorphic allele is required for a synthetic lethal screen. We chose two alleles, dna2-1, a ts mutant sensitive to a variety of DNA damaging agents, and dna2-2, a mutant that grows at 23 degreesC and 37 degreesC, but is sensitive to MMS, bleomycin, and X-rays [8,20]. dna2-1 contains a P504S substitution in a region of the protein N-terminal to both the nuclease and helicase domains [3]. All enzymatic activities of the Dna2-1 protein are reduced relative to wild-type (WT)-DNA-stimulated ATPase, DNA helicase, and single-stranded DNA nuclease activity [21]. The dna2-2 mutation changes arginine at position 1235, an invariant residue in helicase region IV, to glutamine [8]. A crystal structure of PCR helicase shows that residues in region IV bind the adenine base of ATP [22]. The dna2-1 strain grows very slowly, even at the permissive temperature, so synthetic sickness is sometimes difficult to unambiguously assign for this mutant. The dna2-2 mutant grows faster than the dna2-1 mutant, and synthetic sickness, characterized by slow growth, can be assigned with greater confidence using dna2-2 strains. The use of each dna2 allele in a separate SGA screen expands the range of detectable synthetic lethal interactions.
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 0 7 0 7 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 80 86 80 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>

###xml 942 947 918 923 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol1,</italic>

###xml 1139 1143 1087 1091 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sae2</italic>
###xml 1150 1154 1094 1098 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mms1</italic>
###xml 1161 1166 1101 1106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mms22</italic>
###xml 1173 1178 1109 1114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">slx5,</italic>
###xml 1183 1189 1119 1125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">slx8),</italic>
###xml 1240 1244 1176 1180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1</italic>
###xml 1251 1256 1183 1188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm3,</italic>
###xml 1261 1265 1193 1197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tof1</italic>
###xml 1313 1317 1241 1245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ctf4</italic>
###xml 1327 1332 1251 1256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ctf18</italic>
###xml 1433 1444 1353 1364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spt16, pob3</italic>
###xml 1446 1450 1366 1370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad6</italic>
###xml 1457 1461 1373 1377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bre1</italic>
###xml 1468 1472 1380 1384 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">swd1</italic>
###xml 1479 1483 1387 1391 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">swd3</italic>
###xml 1490 1494 1394 1398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hst3</italic>
###xml 1501 1505 1401 1405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpd3</italic>
###xml 1512 1517 1408 1413 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pho23</italic>
###xml 1524 1528 1416 1420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rtf1</italic>
###xml 1561 1565 1449 1453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">asf1</italic>
###xml 1622 1626 1506 1510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys7</italic>
###xml 1636 1640 1516 1520 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sod1</italic>
###xml 1687 1691 1563 1567 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hog1</italic>
###xml 1758 1762 1630 1634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ubc4</italic>
###xml 1796 1800 1664 1668 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cla4</italic>
###xml 1832 1836 1696 1700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 1846 1852 1706 1712 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rtt103</italic>
###xml 1884 1888 1740 1744 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1946 1954 1802 1810 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mcm10&#8211;1,</italic>
###xml 1994 1996 1850 1852 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b023">23</xref>
###xml 1999 2004 1855 1860 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdc9,</italic>
###xml 2020 2022 1876 1878 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b024">24</xref>
###xml 2044 2045 1900 1901 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b008">8</xref>
###xml 2049 2054 1905 1910 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpa1,</italic>
###xml 2094 2096 1950 1952 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b013">13</xref>
###xml 2103 2108 1959 1964 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spt16</italic>
###xml 2113 2118 1969 1974 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pob3,</italic>
###xml 2164 2165 2020 2021 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b008">8</xref>
Table 1 lists the validated synthetic lethal and synthetic sick interactions of dna2-1 and dna2-2 strains obtained from the SGA screen (see Materials and Methods). Validation was performed by preparing a new heterozygous diploid between the respective dna2 allele and the candidate gene, followed by sporulation and tetrad dissection. The dna2-allele specificity of some of the interactions may turn out to be significant, as the mutations differentially affect helicase and nuclease activity. Mutants that appeared to show growth defects in the primary screen but that did not meet the stringent requirements (see Materials and Methods) for interaction imposed by the secondary tetrad analysis are found in Table S1. Mutants synthetically lethal or synthetically sick with either dna2-1 or dna2-2 fall into the following categories: genes involved in OFP (rad27Delta, exo1Delta, yen1Delta, rnh35Delta, rnh202Delta, pol3-01, rpa1, elg1Delta, pol1, and pri1), nonessential helicases involved in maintaining chromosome stability (sgs1Delta, srs2Delta, and rrm3Delta), genes involved in repair (rad52Delta, mre11Delta, rad50Delta, xrs2Delta, sae2Delta, mms1Delta, mms22Delta, slx5, and slx8), genes involved in the DNA replication checkpoint (mrc1Delta, csm3, and tof1Delta), genes involved in chromosomal cohesion (ctf4Delta and ctf18Delta), genes involved in chromatin disassembly/assembly and nucleosome modification and remodeling (spt16, pob3, rad6Delta, bre1Delta, swd1Delta, swd3Delta, hst3Delta, rpd3Delta, pho23Delta, rtf1Delta, and the histone chaperone asf1Delta), genes involved in the oxidative stress response (lys7Delta and sod1Delta), a gene in the osmotic stress response (hog1Delta), and genes involved in degradation of short-lived proteins (ubc4Delta), in polarized cell growth (cla4Delta), and in mRNA processing (trf4Delta and rtt103Delta). Previous studies showed dna2 to be synthetically lethal with several essential genes: mcm10-1, involved in initiation of replication [23]; cdc9, a DNA ligase ([24], although see also [8]); rpa1, a single-stranded DNA binding protein [13]; and spt16 and pob3, two genes involved in chromosome remodeling [8].
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 45 49 45 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 123 125 123 125 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b018">18</xref>
###xml 128 136 128 136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 282 286 282 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 299 301 299 301 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b018">18</xref>
###xml 304 312 304 312 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 420 457 420 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2, RAD27, SGS1, SRS2 (HPR5), RRM3,</italic>
###xml 462 467 462 467 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">POL32</italic>
###xml 611 615 611 615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ctf4</italic>
###xml 730 738 726 734 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 770 774 766 770 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">clb2</italic>
###xml 781 785 773 777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">clb3</italic>
###xml 792 796 780 784 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">clb5</italic>
###xml 803 807 787 791 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mad1</italic>
###xml 814 818 794 798 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mad2</italic>
###xml 825 829 801 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mad3</italic>
###xml 836 840 808 812 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bub1</italic>
###xml 847 851 815 819 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bub2</italic>
###xml 862 866 826 830 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bub3</italic>
###xml 873 875 833 835 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b018">18</xref>
###xml 884 888 844 848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CTF4</italic>
###xml 1025 1033 985 993 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen-0010061-st002">Table S2</xref>
###xml 1203 1207 1163 1167 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
The total number of genes that interact with dna2 to date is 56, a connectivity similar to that found in previous screens [18]. Figure 1 shows two-dimensional hierarchical clustering of the data from the current screen and that of previous screens using 43 genes that interact with DNA2 as queries [18]. Figure 2 provides a graphical representation of the network (consisting of 322 genes and 876 interactions) in which DNA2, RAD27, SGS1, SRS2 (HPR5), RRM3, and POL32 form the six major hubs (largest number of connections). We were surprised that none of these genes showed interactions with cell cycle genes. ctf4Delta, however, which is synthetically lethal with all six of these hub genes and many of the other nodes as well (Figure 2), is synthetically lethal with clb2Delta, clb3Delta, clb5Delta, mad1Delta, mad2Delta, mad3Delta, bub1Delta, bub2Delta, and bub3Delta [18]. Thus, CTF4 may provide a missing link between hub genes and cell cycle and kinetochore functions. The same information is shown in tabular form in Table S2, which contains the interacting genes organized by functional categories defined in the MIPS database (). Mutations (identified in studies reported below) that suppress dna2 alleles are also included. We propose that the genes showing the greatest number of interactions encode products that share at least one substrate or have at least one overlapping function.
###end p 14
###begin title 15
Okazaki Fragment Processing
###end title 15
###begin p 16
###xml 60 61 60 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">,</italic>
###xml 191 195 191 195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 320 326 320 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 411 416 411 416 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnh35</italic>
###xml 426 432 422 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnh202</italic>
###xml 468 470 460 462 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b025">25</xref>
###xml 461 466 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Although Dna2p is commonly considered to be required for OFP, this role is far from established. We were therefore interested to find that the SGA experiments identified interactions between DNA2 and additional structure-specific nucleases that, like FEN1, are thought to be involved in overlapping OFP pathways. First, dna2-1 was found to be synthetically lethal with mutations in genes encoding two subunits, rnh35Delta and rnh202Delta, of the main RNaseH in yeast [25], suggesting that Dna2p may be involved in an OFP pathway redundant with RNaseH2.
###end p 16
###begin p 17
###xml 8 14 8 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 119 130 119 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD27, exo1</italic>
###xml 140 144 136 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yen1</italic>
###xml 151 155 143 147 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EXO1</italic>
###xml 217 222 209 214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 228 232 216 220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">exo1</italic>
###xml 320 324 304 308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EXO1</italic>
###xml 353 358 337 342 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 373 375 353 355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b026">26</xref>
###xml 376 378 356 358 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b028">28</xref>
###xml 399 403 379 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EXO1</italic>
###xml 451 457 431 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 505 513 479 487 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 543 545 511 513 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b021">21</xref>
###xml 718 720 686 688 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b029">29</xref>
Second, dna2-2 was synthetically lethal with mutations in genes encoding two exo-endonucleases structurally related to RAD27, exo1Delta and yen1Delta. EXO1 is thought to provide backup function for FEN1 in OFP, since rad27Delta exo1Delta is synthetically lethal (in some genetic backgrounds) and since overexpression of EXO1 suppresses the ts growth of rad27Delta mutants [26-28]. Overexpression of EXO1 also suppressed the temperature sensitivity of dna2-1 at the restrictive temperature of 30 degreesC (Figure 3), though not at 37 degreesC [21]. Exo1p nuclease acts on 5' flap-containing structures, and these genetic interactions suggest that such flaps may be the common in vivo substrate of both Dna2p and Exo1p [29].
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 19 25 19 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 53 57 53 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yen1</italic>
###xml 376 380 360 364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yen1</italic>
###xml 452 456 432 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yen1</italic>
###xml 462 466 438 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">exo1</italic>
###xml 472 476 444 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">din7</italic>
###xml 482 486 450 454 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad2</italic>
###xml 558 560 510 512 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b026">26</xref>
###xml 588 592 540 544 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 641 645 593 597 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yen1</italic>
###xml 661 665 609 613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yen1</italic>
###xml 783 794 731 742 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen-0010061-sd001">Protocol S1</xref>
We also found that dna2-2 is synthetically sick with yen1Delta at 30 degreesC and lethal, i.e., ts, at 37 degreesC. Yen1p shows 23% identity with Rad27p, 33% identity with Rad2p (founding member of this nuclease family and involved in nucleotide excision repair), and 24% identity with Din7p (Rad2p-like endonuclease proposed to be involved in mitochondrial mismatch repair). yen1Delta mutants do not appear to have DNA damage or growth defects, and a yen1Delta exo1Delta din7Delta rad2Delta mutant has no growth defect at either 30 degreesC or 37 degreesC [26]. Synthetic lethality with dna2 is the first informative phenotype reported for yen1Delta, although yen1 is synthetically lethal with another gene that is in turn synthetically lethal with several replication mutants (see Protocol S1).
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 110 112 110 112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b017">17</xref>
###xml 113 115 113 115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b030">30</xref>
###xml 116 118 116 118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b031">31</xref>
###xml 121 125 121 125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">elg1</italic>
###xml 131 137 127 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 172 179 168 175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 410 416 406 412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 451 456 447 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ctf18</italic>
###xml 463 464 455 456 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b008">8</xref>
###xml 480 485 472 477 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad24</italic>
###xml 527 531 515 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">elg1</italic>
###xml 644 646 628 630 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b030">30</xref>
###xml 647 649 631 633 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b032">32</xref>
Elg1p, like Dna2p, is proposed to be involved in OFP, as well as in telomere silencing and length regulation [17,30,31]. elg1Delta dna2-1 mutants are synthetically lethal (Table 1). Elg1p is homologous to Rfc1p (the large subunit of the replication factor C clamp loader), to Rad24p (a Rfc1p homolog required for DNA damage checkpoints), and to Ctf18p (another Rfc1p homolog involved in chromosomal cohesion). dna2-2 is also synthetically lethal with ctf18Delta [8], but not with rad24Delta (this work). S phase progression in elg1Delta mutants is slower than in WT strains, suggesting that Elg1p is involved in replication fork translocation [30-32].
###end p 19
###begin title 20
###xml 15 19 15 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
Interaction of dna2 with Pol delta
###end title 20
###begin p 21
###xml 277 279 273 275 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b010">10</xref>
###xml 280 282 276 278 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b012">12</xref>
###xml 283 285 279 281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b014">14</xref>
###xml 286 288 282 284 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b033">33</xref>
###xml 483 487 479 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 568 574 564 570 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 588 596 584 592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3&#8211;01,</italic>
###xml 669 671 661 663 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b033">33</xref>
###xml 686 694 678 686 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 696 710 688 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 797 811 789 803 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3&#8211;01 dna2&#8211;1</italic>
It has been proposed, based on in vitro biochemical reconstitution in vitro, that not all Okazaki fragments require Dna2p for processing. Instead, the in vivo substrates of Dna2p are only those Okazaki fragments on which pol delta produces 5' flaps longer than 30 nucleotides [10,12,14,33]. We wished to devise a genetic test of this hypothesis. One way to do so is by generating excessive strand displacement in vivo and assessing whether there is then an increased requirement for DNA2. This was accomplished by testing the viability of a strain containing both the dna2-1 mutation and pol3-01, a mutation in pol delta known to increase strand displacement in vitro [33]. As shown in Figure 4, dna2-1 pol3-01 is synthetically lethal. We propose that excessive strand displacement in vivo in the pol3-01 dna2-1 strain causes the lethality, supporting the predictions from purely biochemical reconstitution.
###end p 21
###begin p 22
###xml 34 39 30 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 75 80 67 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 139 144 127 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 172 177 156 161 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 184 188 164 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3</italic>
###xml 195 199 171 175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sgs1</italic>
###xml 210 214 182 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">srs2</italic>
###xml 262 266 230 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 272 280 240 248 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 306 311 274 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 372 384 336 348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 pol32</italic>
###xml 456 461 416 421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 511 517 467 473 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 586 592 536 542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 616 624 560 568 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 632 637 576 581 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 690 696 630 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 720 728 654 662 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 753 757 687 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 784 789 718 723 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 863 869 793 799 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 874 880 804 810 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 890 898 820 828 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 904 905 834 835 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g005">5</xref>
###xml 923 928 853 858 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 1000 1004 926 930 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1014 1020 940 946 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1025 1031 951 957 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1075 1080 1001 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 1159 1171 1081 1093 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 pol32</italic>
###xml 1181 1193 1099 1111 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 pol32</italic>
###xml 1241 1246 1155 1160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 1275 1281 1185 1191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1285 1291 1195 1201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1301 1309 1211 1219 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 1315 1316 1225 1226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g005">5</xref>
###xml 1433 1435 1335 1337 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b034">34</xref>
###xml 1570 1575 1468 1473 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2,</italic>
###xml 1741 1745 1635 1639 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1750 1757 1644 1651 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 1781 1787 1675 1681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1791 1796 1685 1690 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 1922 1932 1812 1822 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
Another pol delta subunit mutant, pol32Delta, is synthetically lethal with rad27Delta, and the network of synthetic lethal interactions of pol32Delta is similar to that of rad27Delta, rrm3Delta, sgs1Delta, and srs2Delta, which are also synthetically lethal with dna2 (See Figure 2). We were surprised that pol32Delta did not show up in our SGA screen, and directly tested dna2-1 pol32Delta for synthetic lethality. Rather than showing synthetic lethality, pol32Delta suppressed the slow growth phenotype of the dna2-1 strain at 23 degreesC and suppressed the ts growth phenotype of the dna2-1 strain at 30 degreesC (Figure 5A). The pol32Delta mutation did not suppress the lethality of the dna2-1 strain at 37 degreesC (Figure 5A) or the lethality of a DNA2 deletion (not shown). The pol32Delta deletion mutation also suppressed the DNA damage sensitivity of the dna2-1 and dna2-2 mutants (Figure 5B and 5C, respectively). pol32Delta mutants are sensitive to different concentrations of MMS than are dna2 mutants. dna2-1 and dna2-2 mutants are sensitive to 0.005% MMS, while pol32Delta strains are resistant to 0.005% MMS but are sensitive to 0.01% MMS. Both dna2-1 pol32Delta and dna2-2 pol32Delta mutants showed MMS sensitivity similar to pol32Delta strains rather than to dna2-1 or dna2-2 strains (Figure 5B and 5C). Pol32p is a nonessential subunit of the pol delta holoenzyme and is required for full processivity of pol delta [34]. Therefore, a less processive pol delta suppresses the growth and repair defects of both nuclease- and helicase-deficient mutants of dna2, suggesting that Dna2p is acting on flaps arising from excessive strand displacement by pol delta during DNA repair as well as during OFP. The synthetic lethality of dna2 and pol3-01 and the suppression of dna2-1 by pol32Delta provide strong genetic evidence that the Dna2p substrates shown to be optimal in vitro are also substrates in vivo (see Discussion).
###end p 22
###begin title 23
The Helicase Network
###end title 23
###begin p 24
###xml 33 39 33 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 69 73 69 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sgs1</italic>
###xml 80 84 76 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">srs2</italic>
###xml 95 99 87 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3</italic>
###xml 106 108 94 96 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b035">35</xref>
###xml 109 111 97 99 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b037">37</xref>
###xml 256 260 244 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 306 310 294 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sgs1</italic>
###xml 320 324 304 308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">srs2</italic>
###xml 343 352 323 332 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g001">Figures 1</xref>
###xml 357 358 337 338 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g002">2</xref>
We have reported previously that dna2-2 is synthetically lethal with sgs1Delta, srs2Delta, and rrm3Delta [35-37], and our SGA screen also detected these genes. More significantly, there is extensive overlap between genes that are synthetically lethal with dna2 and those that are synthetically lethal with sgs1Delta and srs2Delta, as shown in Figures 1 and 2.
###end p 24
###begin p 25
###xml 148 152 148 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 185 192 185 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 568 570 568 570 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b038">38</xref>
###xml 612 623 612 623 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 sgs1</italic>
###xml 630 641 626 637 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 srs2</italic>
###xml 652 663 644 655 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rrm3</italic>
###xml 687 694 675 682 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 696 707 684 695 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 sgs1</italic>
###xml 717 728 701 712 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 srs2</italic>
###xml 834 839 814 819 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad51</italic>
###xml 874 876 850 852 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b035">35</xref>
###xml 877 879 853 855 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b037">37</xref>
###xml 886 896 862 872 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
###xml 928 944 904 916 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rrm3&#916;</italic>
###xml 1017 1024 989 996 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 1061 1072 1033 1044 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rrm3</italic>
To assess the functional relationship between Dna2p and these helicases, we have tried to further determine whether the synthetic lethality between dna2 and the helicase genes shown in Table 2 stems from defects in DNA replication per se or from the aberrant DNA structures that arise during repair of DNA replication errors. Towards this end, we first checked whether the lethality was suppressed by mutations in genes considered necessary for resolving potentially lethal intermediates that form when the original lesions enter the recombination pathway for repair [38]. The results of our current analysis of dna2-2 sgs1Delta, dna2-2 srs2Delta, and dna2-2 rrm3Delta are summarized in Table 2. dna2-2 sgs1Delta and dna2-2 srs2Delta were synthetically lethal and were either inefficiently or efficiently suppressed, respectively, by rad51Delta, as we reported previously ([35,37]; see Discussion). New here is the finding that dna2-2 rrm3Delta lethality was not suppressed by mutations in the recombination pathway (Table 2). This indicates that cell death in dna2-2 rrm3Delta does not result from the accumulation of nonresolvable recombination intermediates but from the formation of early replication intermediates, or possibly blocked DNA replication forks.
###end p 25
###begin p 26
###xml 60 79 60 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">(MMS4/SLX3, SLX1/4,</italic>
###xml 84 92 84 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SLD5/8),</italic>
###xml 175 179 175 179 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SGS1</italic>
###xml 225 227 225 227 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b039">39</xref>
###xml 283 287 283 287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">slx5</italic>
###xml 297 301 293 297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">slx8</italic>
###xml 349 353 341 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
Gene pairs encoding three different heterodimeric complexes (MMS4/SLX3, SLX1/4, and SLD5/8), although they are not DNA helicases, are required for viability in the absence of SGS1 and, thus, are part of the helicase network [39]. We find that only one of these complexes, defined by slx5Delta and slx8Delta, shows synthetic lethal interactions with dna2. Since the function of the Slx5/8p complex is unknown, we cannot yet predict the nature of the substrates that might be shared with Dna2p.
###end p 26
###begin title 27
DNA Repair
###end title 27
###begin p 28
###xml 30 34 30 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 39 44 39 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad52</italic>
###xml 82 84 78 80 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b016">16</xref>
###xml 87 92 83 88 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad52</italic>
###xml 140 144 132 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 284 288 276 280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 349 354 341 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 406 418 394 406 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 rad51</italic>
###xml 428 440 412 424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 rad55</italic>
###xml 458 470 438 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rad51</italic>
###xml 480 484 456 460 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 487 492 463 468 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad59</italic>
###xml 651 663 623 635 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rad51</italic>
###xml 669 674 637 642 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad59</italic>
###xml 826 830 790 794 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MMS1</italic>
###xml 835 840 799 804 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MMS22</italic>
###xml 979 983 943 947 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1036 1038 1000 1002 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b040">40</xref>
###xml 1111 1123 1075 1087 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rad52</italic>
We have previously shown that dna2 and rad52Delta mutants are synthetically sick [16]. rad52Delta also appeared synthetically sick with the dna2 alleles in the SGA screen. We were surprised that other genes required for recombinational repair did not appear synthetically lethal with dna2 in the SGA screen, since they are synthetically lethal with rad27Delta. To insure that we had not missed such genes, dna2-1 rad51Delta and dna2-1 rad55Delta, as well as dna2-2 rad51Delta and dna2-2 rad59Delta, mutants were constructed. Consistent with the global screen, these double mutants did not appear to be synthetically lethal or sick. We also found that dna2-2 rad51Delta rad59Delta triple mutants were viable (not shown). Our results indicate that the Rad51p/Rad59p portion of the Rad52p pathway does not buffer Dna2p function. MMS1 and MMS22 are two additional presumed DNA repair genes that are also required for normal S phase progression and that show synthetic lethality with dna2 mutants in the SGA screen, as previously described [40]. The Mms1p/Mms22p system may correspond to the pathway that results in dna2-2 rad52Delta growth defects.
###end p 28
###begin p 29
###xml 29 35 29 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 40 47 40 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad50&#8211;5</italic>
###xml 101 103 101 103 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b016">16</xref>
###xml 162 172 162 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 mre11</italic>
###xml 182 192 178 188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 rad50</italic>
###xml 236 243 228 235 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 246 253 238 245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad50&#8211;5</italic>
###xml 277 282 269 274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD50</italic>
###xml 331 336 323 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad50</italic>
###xml 347 352 335 340 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad52</italic>
###xml 476 490 460 474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rad50&#8211;5</italic>
###xml 518 530 502 514 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rad50</italic>
###xml 556 569 536 549 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MRE11, RAD50,</italic>
###xml 574 578 554 558 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XRS2</italic>
###xml 762 764 742 744 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b041">41</xref>
###xml 765 767 745 747 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b042">42</xref>
###xml 803 807 783 787 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">xrs2</italic>
###xml 871 882 847 858 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 xrs2</italic>
Previously, we reported that dna2-2 and rad50-5 double mutants were viable and epistatic for repair [16]. Therefore, one of our most unexpected findings was that dna2 mre11Delta and dna2 rad50Delta strains are synthetically lethal (see Table 1). rad50-5 is a point mutation of RAD50 that is as sensitive to irradiation as either a rad50Delta or a rad52Delta strain. Clearly, some function must remain in the point mutant as compared to the deletion mutant, however, since the dna2-2 rad50-5 strain is viable while the dna2-2 rad50Delta strain is inviable. MRE11, RAD50, and XRS2 encode members of the Mre11p complex, which is required for the intra-S phase checkpoint, for homologous recombination, for non-homologous end joining, and for telomere maintenance ([41,42] and references therein). Although xrs2Delta was not found in our SGA screen, we have since shown that dna2-2 xrs2Delta is synthetically lethal (this work).
###end p 29
###begin title 30
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 32 49 32 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad9, mrc1, mec1,</italic>
###xml 53 57 53 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tel1</italic>
dna2 Mutants Do Not Require the rad9, mrc1, mec1, or tel1 Checkpoint Activities for Viability
###end title 30
###begin p 31
###xml 40 44 40 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 91 97 91 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 102 108 102 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 145 150 145 150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 194 198 190 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 254 259 250 255 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad9,</italic>
###xml 330 331 326 327 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b008">8</xref>
###xml 332 334 328 330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b043">43</xref>
###xml 346 350 342 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 360 365 356 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 409 413 401 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad9</italic>
###xml 418 419 406 407 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">.</italic>
###xml 433 438 421 426 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 516 521 500 505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad24</italic>
###xml 531 536 511 516 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad17</italic>
###xml 658 668 634 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 rad24</italic>
###xml 678 688 650 660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 rad17</italic>
###xml 728 734 696 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">, dna2</italic>
Our analysis of the interaction between dna2 and checkpoint mutants supports the view that dna2-1 and dna2-2 mutants accumulate less damage than rad27Delta mutants. First, we found that neither dna2 allele used in our screen is synthetically lethal with rad9, a mediator of the intra-S DNA damage checkpoint, as found previously [8,43] for other dna2 alleles. rad27Delta mutants are synthetically lethal with rad9Delta. In addition, rad27Delta mutants are synthetically lethal with the DNA damage checkpoint mutants rad24Delta and rad17Delta, which represent the checkpoint clamp-loader-like complex and the checkpoint clamp-like proteins, respectively, but dna2 rad24Delta and dna2 rad17Delta are both viable (this study). Thus, dna2 mutants do not accumulate sufficient damage to require the intra-S DNA damage checkpoint for viability at the permissive temperature.
###end p 31
###begin p 32
###xml 47 51 47 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 90 94 90 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1</italic>
###xml 101 105 97 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tof1</italic>
###xml 115 119 107 111 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">csm3</italic>
###xml 126 133 114 121 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 412 414 400 402 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b018">18</xref>
###xml 564 566 552 554 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b044">44</xref>
###xml 567 569 555 557 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b045">45</xref>
###xml 572 581 560 569 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 mrc1</italic>
###xml 655 659 639 643 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 735 737 719 721 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b043">43</xref>
###xml 832 836 816 820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MRC1</italic>
###xml 838 842 822 826 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MRC1</italic>
###xml 847 851 831 835 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TOF1</italic>
###xml 937 941 921 925 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1</italic>
###xml 1050 1052 1030 1032 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b046">46</xref>
###xml 1075 1077 1055 1057 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b045">45</xref>
###xml 1116 1120 1096 1100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1</italic>
###xml 1222 1228 1202 1208 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1AQ</italic>
###xml 1235 1239 1215 1219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1</italic>
###xml 1338 1349 1314 1325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1AQ rad9</italic>
###xml 1403 1409 1375 1381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1AQ</italic>
###xml 1450 1456 1422 1428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1AQ</italic>
###xml 1516 1520 1488 1492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1</italic>
###xml 1546 1555 1514 1523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 mrc1</italic>
###xml 1582 1595 1546 1559 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 mrc1AQ</italic>
###xml 1600 1613 1564 1577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 mrc1AQ</italic>
###xml 1776 1780 1740 1744 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1801 1809 1765 1773 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 1837 1841 1801 1805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD9</italic>
###xml 1867 1871 1831 1835 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MRC1</italic>
###xml 1879 1892 1843 1856 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 mrc1AQ</italic>
###xml 1901 1919 1865 1883 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 mrc1AQ rad9</italic>
###xml 2019 2027 1979 1987 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 2047 2065 2007 2025 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 mrc1AQ rad9</italic>
###xml 2143 2147 2099 2103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MRC1</italic>
###xml 2199 2208 2155 2164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 mrc1</italic>
###xml 884 889 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
We found in the SGA experiments, however, that dna2 mutants are synthetically lethal with mrc1Delta, tof1Delta, or csm3Delta (Table 1). These genes define a checkpoint pathway thought to operate in parallel with the Rad9p pathway to respond specifically to replication stress. Mrc1p, Tof1p, and Csm3p are required for Rad53p phosphorylation in the presence of HU or MMS, both of which induce S phase DNA damage [18]. Mrc1p is an adapter molecule in the checkpoint, whose phosphorylation by Mec1p at SQ/TQ motifs is required for activation of downstream effectors [44,45]. dna2 mrc1Delta synthetic lethality seemed to contradict the observation that other dna2 alleles actually show improved survival in the absence of the checkpoint ([43]; see below), and suggested that such synthetic lethality might be due to another function of MRC1. MRC1 and TOF1 appear to play a direct role in yeast DNA replication, as well as in the checkpoint. mrc1Delta strains also show a slow S phase, and Mrc1p and Tof1p have been localized to moving replication forks [46]. Osborn and Elledge [45] constructed a separation-of-function mrc1 mutant that has all 17 TQ and SQ Mec1p target sites mutated to non-phosphorylatable AQ. This mutant, mrc1AQ, like mrc1Delta, is checkpoint defective, as evidenced by the fact that Rad53p phosphorylation is blocked in mrc1AQ rad9Delta mutants upon treatment with HU or MMS. However, mrc1AQ mutants are replication proficient. The mrc1AQ mutant allowed us to ask whether the replication defect of mrc1Delta was responsible for dna2 mrc1Delta synthetic lethality. dna2-1 mrc1AQ and dna2-2 mrc1AQ strains were constructed and were viable and did not appear synthetically sick, indicating that the checkpoint function of Mrc1p is not required for viability in dna2 mutant backgrounds (Figure 6). In order to be sure that RAD9 was not substituting for MRC1 in the dna2-2 mrc1AQ mutant, dna2-2 mrc1AQ rad9Delta mutants, which lack both the DNA damage and replication stress checkpoints, were constructed (Figure 6). The viability of dna2-2 mrc1AQ rad9Delta strains suggests that it is inactivation of the replication function of MRC1 that is responsible for synthetic lethality in the dna2 mrc1Delta mutants.
###end p 32
###begin p 33
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1</italic>
###xml 14 18 10 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3</italic>
###xml 63 65 55 57 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b047">47</xref>
###xml 80 84 72 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RRM3</italic>
###xml 89 93 81 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 108 115 100 107 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 139 143 131 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1</italic>
###xml 149 158 137 142 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3&#916;</italic>
###xml 232 243 216 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mrc1AQ rrm3</italic>
###xml 313 321 293 301 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g006">Figure 6</xref>
