###xml 330 334 310 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 339 343 319 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3</italic>
###xml 394 398 374 378 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 400 405 380 385 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RRM3,</italic>
###xml 410 414 390 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MRC1</italic>
mrc1Delta and rrm3Delta mutants are also synthetically lethal [47] and, because RRM3 and DNA2 interact (see Table 2), we asked whether the mrc1Delta rrm3Delta synthetic lethality is caused by a checkpoint or replication defect. The mrc1AQ rrm3Delta double mutants showed the same viability as the single mutants (Figure 6). Since dna2 and rrm3 are also synthetically lethal, this suggests that DNA2, RRM3, and MRC1 functions may be interdependent in DNA replication.
###end p 33
###begin p 34
###xml 78 82 78 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 120 124 120 124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 130 139 130 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1&#916;</italic>
###xml 144 153 140 145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tel1&#916;</italic>
###xml 186 190 178 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MRC1</italic>
###xml 195 199 187 191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD9</italic>
###xml 240 256 232 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2/DNA2 tel1</italic>
###xml 262 271 250 259 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TEL1 mec1</italic>
###xml 277 286 261 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1 sml1</italic>
###xml 292 296 272 276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SML1</italic>
###xml 330 338 310 318 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen-0010061-st003">Table S3</xref>
###xml 388 392 368 372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 409 413 385 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 435 439 407 411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 504 510 472 478 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 553 560 521 528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;20</italic>
###xml 562 564 530 532 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b043">43</xref>
###xml 619 625 587 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 634 642 602 610 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 649 653 617 621 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tel1</italic>
###xml 714 720 678 684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 737 745 695 703 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 777 783 735 741 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 788 792 746 750 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tel1</italic>
###xml 913 915 867 869 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b048">48</xref>
###xml 918 929 872 883 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 tel1</italic>
###xml 935 939 885 889 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 988 996 934 942 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 1011 1022 957 968 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 tel1</italic>
###xml 1028 1032 970 974 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 1132 1136 1070 1074 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 1142 1146 1076 1080 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tel1</italic>
###xml 1194 1198 1124 1128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">est2</italic>
###xml 1252 1254 1178 1180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b049">49</xref>
###xml 1261 1267 1187 1193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1408 1419 1334 1345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 tel1</italic>
###xml 1425 1429 1347 1351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 1470 1481 1388 1399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 est2</italic>
###xml 1542 1544 1456 1458 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b017">17</xref>
To further test the idea that S phase checkpoint signaling is dispensable for dna2 mutant viability, the interaction of dna2 with mec1Delta and tel1Delta, mutations in genes upstream of MRC1 and RAD9 in the checkpoint, were investigated. A dna2-2/DNA2 tel1Delta/TEL1 mec1Delta/MEC1 sml1Delta/SML1 heterozygote was sporulated, and Table S3 lists the genotypes obtained among the tetrads. (sml1Delta allows for mec1Delta viability.) The mec1Delta mutation partially suppressed the slow growth phenotype of dna2-2 strains. Thus, as previously observed for dna2-20 [43], the Mec1p-mediated checkpoint is deleterious in the dna2-2 mutant (Figure 7). The tel1Delta mutation shows negative synergy but not lethality with dna2-2 at 37 degreesC (Figure 7). The negative synergy between dna2-2 and tel1Delta is evidence that Dna2p and Tel1p may function together at DSBs and/or at telomeres, along with the Mre11p complex [48]. dna2-2 tel1Delta mec1Delta triple mutants were recovered. As shown in Figure 7, however, the dna2-2 tel1Delta mec1Delta mutant grew more slowly than any of the single or double mutants. The telomere defects of the mec1Delta tel1Delta strain caused it to senesce as rapidly as est2Delta (telomerase catalytic subunit deleted) strains [49]. The dna2-2 mutation may cause additional defects in telomere replication. Thus, enhanced telomeric senescence might account for the slow growth of the dna2-2 tel1Delta mec1Delta mutant, just as we have shown that dna2-2 est2Delta is synthetically lethal due to accelerated senescence [17].
###end p 34
###begin p 35
###xml 38 42 38 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 79 84 79 84 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD53</italic>
###xml 97 103 97 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 108 114 108 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 130 135 130 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad53</italic>
###xml 141 145 137 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 159 171 151 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 rad53</italic>
###xml 177 181 165 169 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 191 203 175 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rad53</italic>
###xml 209 213 189 193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 263 273 239 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 rad53</italic>
###xml 334 338 310 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 414 420 390 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 607 611 583 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MEC1</italic>
Finally, we tested the interaction of DNA2 with the checkpoint effector kinase RAD53. We crossed dna2-1 and dna2-2 to an isogenic rad53Delta sml1Delta strain. dna2-1 rad53Delta sml1Delta and dna2-2 rad53Delta sml1Delta mutants were fully viable. The viability of dna2 rad53 strengthens the conclusion that the DNA damage arising in a dna2 mutant is not sufficient to require the S phase checkpoint for viability. (dna2-1 mutants, however, do induce an amount of damage above the threshold for checkpoint activation at restrictive temperatures, since they arrest at the metaphase to anaphase transition in a MEC1-dependent manner [M. E. B. and J. L. C., unpublished data].)
###end p 35
###begin title 36
Sister Chromatid Cohesion and Repair of DSBs in the rDNA
###end title 36
###begin p 37
###xml 38 40 34 36 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b050">50</xref>
###xml 47 51 43 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ctf4</italic>
###xml 109 111 101 103 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b020">20</xref>
###xml 114 120 106 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 174 178 166 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ctf4</italic>
###xml 208 212 196 200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 252 254 240 242 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b051">51</xref>
###xml 289 293 277 281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 294 295 282 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</italic>
###xml 417 422 405 410 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FOB1,</italic>
###xml 582 588 570 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 704 708 692 696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fob1</italic>
###xml 726 737 710 721 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 ctf4</italic>
###xml 795 806 775 786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 ctf4</italic>
###xml 812 816 788 792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fob1</italic>
###xml 883 894 849 860 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 ctf4</italic>
###xml 900 904 862 866 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fob1</italic>
###xml 997 1006 955 964 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 ctf4</italic>
###xml 1012 1016 966 970 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fob1</italic>
###xml 1147 1155 1079 1087 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 1276 1283 1208 1215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2,</italic>
Ctf4p is a pol alpha-binding protein [50], and ctf4Delta strains are defective in sister chromatid cohesion [20]. dna2-2 was identified as a mutant synthetically lethal with ctf4Delta, but we have shown that dna2 mutants are not defective in cohesion [51]. We previously reported that the dna2-2 mutation gave rise to an increased frequency of DSBs at the replication fork barrier (RFB) in the rDNA and that deleting FOB1, which is required for pausing at the RFB, suppressed DSB formation. A reasonable explanation for all of these observations is that the DSB damage sustained by dna2-2 mutants at the RFB might require Ctf4p-mediated sister chromatid cohesion for repair. If so, then one would expect fob1Delta to suppress dna2-2 ctf4Delta synthetic lethality. We dissected 55 tetrads from a dna2-2 ctf4Delta fob1Delta heterozygote and incubated the spores at 30 degreesC. Viable dna2-2 ctf4Delta fob1Delta mutants were obtained in the expected numbers, demonstrating suppression. Although the dna2 ctf4Delta fob1Delta triple mutants grew at 23 degreesC and at 30 degreesC, they did not grow at 37 degreesC and were highly sensitive to X-rays (Figure 8). The behavior of the triple mutant indicates that defects in the rDNA locus are critical for some of the phenotypes of dna2-2, but that defects elsewhere throughout the chromosome must still occur, giving rise to ts growth and DNA damage sensitivity.
###end p 37
###begin title 38
Nucleosome Remodeling: Dna2p Interacts with Pol alpha and Primase
###end title 38
###begin p 39
###xml 123 125 123 125 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b052">52</xref>
###xml 128 134 128 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 183 187 183 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">POB3</italic>
###xml 189 196 189 196 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pob3&#8211;21</italic>
###xml 198 200 198 200 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b052">52</xref>
###xml 226 231 226 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spt16</italic>
###xml 270 276 270 276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 278 280 278 280 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b053">53</xref>
###xml 545 547 541 543 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b054">54</xref>
###xml 548 550 544 546 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b055">55</xref>
###xml 568 572 564 568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 690 696 682 688 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol1&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 729 731 721 723 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b056">56</xref>
###xml 776 782 768 774 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 787 793 779 785 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol1&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 835 848 827 840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 pol1&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 863 876 855 868 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 pol1&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 913 919 905 911 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 953 960 945 952 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol1&#8211;17</italic>
###xml 987 989 979 981 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b057">57</xref>
###xml 996 1006 988 998 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
###xml 1088 1092 1080 1084 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1155 1161 1147 1153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1242 1255 1234 1247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 pol1&#8211;1</italic>
Pob3p and Spt16p/Cdc68p form a heterodimer that is a component of the ATP-independent chromatin remodeling activity yFACT [52]. dna2-2 is synthetically lethal with a non-ts allele of POB3, pob3-21 [52], and various alleles of spt16 are synthetically lethal or sick with dna2-2 [53]. Since yFACT may participate in both DNA replication and transcription, to investigate a potential link with the role of Dna2p in replication and/or repair, we took advantage of the observation that yFACT interacts both genetically and physically with pol alpha [54,55]. This suggested dna2 might be synthetically lethal with a mutant containing a pol alpha protein that fails to interact with Pob3p/Spt16p, pol1-1 (with glycine at position 493) [56]. We established the synthetic lethality of dna2-2 and pol1-1 (18 tetrads, 46 viable spores, no double dna2-2 pol1-1 mutants). The dna2-2 pol1-1 lethality is allele specific, since dna2-1 is not synthetically lethal with pol1-17, a catalytic site mutant [57] (see Discussion). Although yFACT may also affect transcription and the synthetic effects between dna2 and yFACT components could be due to reduced transcription of dna2-2 or of other replication genes in the double mutants, the synthetic lethality of dna2-2 pol1-1 argues that Dna2p and yFACT may interact during DNA replication.
###end p 39
###begin p 40
###xml 55 59 55 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 119 125 115 121 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 181 188 177 184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pri1-M4</italic>
###xml 319 326 315 322 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pri1-M4</italic>
###xml 362 364 358 360 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b058">58</xref>
We went on to investigate genetic interactions between dna2 and genes encoding other pol alpha subunits. We found that dna2-2 is synthetically lethal with a primase subunit mutant, pri1-M4 (18 tetrads, 51 viable spores, no double mutants). This result further implicates Dna2p in lagging-strand DNA replication, as the pri1-M4 mutant is defective in elongation [58].
###end p 40
###begin title 41
Chromatin Remodeling and Histone Modification
###end title 41
###begin p 42
###xml 51 55 51 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 97 101 97 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 102 108 102 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol1&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 277 281 277 281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 343 346 343 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sf1</italic>
###xml 448 452 444 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 645 647 641 643 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b059">59</xref>
In addition to clarifying the relationship between dna2 and the yFACT complex by identifying the dna2/pol1-1 interaction, the SGA screen suggested a role for Dna2p in additional complexes that control assembly and disassembly of chromatin during DNA replication. We found that dna2 mutants are synthetically lethal or synthetically sick with asf1Delta, defective in a chaperone protein involved in histone deposition at the replication fork. Since dna2 mutants are defective in OFP, they might also be defective in the rapid reassembly of chromatin behind the replication fork, leading to an accumulation of defective chromatin and lethal DSBs [59].
###end p 42
###begin p 43
###xml 34 38 34 38 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 85 89 85 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad6</italic>
###xml 96 100 92 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bre1</italic>
###xml 107 111 99 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">swd1</italic>
###xml 122 126 110 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">swd3</italic>
###xml 137 144 121 128 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 274 276 258 260 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b060">60</xref>
###xml 277 279 261 263 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b061">61</xref>
###xml 342 347 326 331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD18</italic>
###xml 379 383 363 367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BRE1</italic>
###xml 415 417 399 401 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b062">62</xref>
###xml 418 420 402 404 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b065">65</xref>
###xml 423 433 407 417 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 rad18</italic>
###xml 487 491 467 471 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 532 536 512 516 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bre1</italic>
###xml 597 607 573 583 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">BRE1, swd1</italic>
###xml 617 621 589 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">swd3</italic>
###xml 628 635 596 603 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 781 790 749 758 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 rad6</italic>
The SGA screen also revealed that dna2 mutants are synthetically lethal or sick with rad6Delta, bre1Delta, swd1Delta, and swd3Delta (see Table 1). Rad6p is a ubiquitin-conjugating enzyme (E2) required for post-replication repair, the N-end rule, and chromatin modification [60,61]. Rad6p functions with two alternative ubiquitin ligases (E3)-RAD18 in post-replication repair and BRE1 in histone H2B ubiquitylation [62-65]. dna2 rad18Delta mutants grew normally (this work). By contrast, dna2 showed synthetic sick interactions with bre1Delta and with mutations in two genes that act downstream of BRE1, swd1Delta and swd3Delta (Table 1). Bre1p-mediated histone H2B ubiquitylation is necessary for histone H3 lysine 4 methylation by Swd1p and Swd3p. These results may indicate that dna2 rad6Delta growth defects do not result from defective post-replication repair, but rather from defects in histone modification.
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 39 43 39 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rtf1</italic>
###xml 116 120 112 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RTF1</italic>
###xml 238 247 234 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 rtf1</italic>
###xml 294 298 286 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 401 405 393 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 449 453 441 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">paf1</italic>
###xml 486 490 474 478 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 550 554 538 542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">paf1</italic>
###xml 760 762 744 746 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b066">66</xref>
###xml 817 821 801 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">paf1</italic>
###xml 846 850 826 830 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rtf1</italic>
dna2 is also synthetically lethal with rtf1Delta, which is involved in recruitment of Set1p and H2B ubiquitylation. RTF1 is a member of the PAF1p complex. Since the PAF1p complex is involved in transcription, a trivial explanation of the dna2 rtf1Delta lethality could be that transcription of dna2 or of another replication gene is reduced and indirectly creates the synthetic lethality. If so, then dna2 should also be synthetically lethal with a paf1Delta. However, we found that no dna2 allele tested was either synthetically sick or lethal with paf1Delta. Recent evidence suggests that Rtf1p, which recruits Set1p, affects genome-wide ubiquitylation of histone H2B by a mechanism that is distinct from its function as a transcriptional elongation factor [66], and that would explain how we can find no effect of paf1Delta but lethality with rtf1Delta.
###end p 44
###begin p 45
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 94 98 94 98 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hst3</italic>
###xml 108 113 104 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pho23</italic>
###xml 264 266 256 258 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b067">67</xref>
###xml 267 269 259 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b068">68</xref>
###xml 296 307 288 299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rpd3</italic>
###xml 358 362 346 350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 434 438 422 426 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpd3</italic>
###xml 462 473 446 457 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen-0010061-sd001">Protocol S1</xref>
###xml 735 739 719 723 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
dna2 also shows synthetic interactions with mutations in genes encoding histone deacetylases: hst3Delta and pho23Delta. Rpd3p and Pho23p are components of a histone deacetylase complex that is thought to be involved in regulation of initiation of DNA replication [67,68], and therefore we tested dna2-2 rpd3Delta, and found that it was synthetically lethal. DNA2 is the only replication gene that has shown a genetic interaction with rpd3Delta to date (see also Protocol S1). (We wish to emphasize that for all of the chromatin-modifying pathways detected in the screen, we have shown, in studies in preparation for presentation elsewhere, that the effects are not due to the trivial explanation of reduced transcription of the mutant dna2 genes).
###end p 45
###begin title 46
Other Interactions
###end title 46
###begin p 47
###xml 138 142 138 142 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trf4</italic>
###xml 152 158 148 154 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rtt103</italic>
###xml 201 205 193 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 237 248 229 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen-0010061-sd001">Protocol S1</xref>
###xml 294 299 286 291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAF20</italic>
Additional nodes in the network (oxidative stress genes, osmotic stress genes, and genes involved in RNA modification/catabolism [mutants trf4Delta and rtt103Delta]) that are synthetically lethal with dna2 are described and discussed in Protocol S1. Genes involved in transcription elongation (CAF20, for example) have not yet been further analyzed because they may reduce transcription of Dna2p or another replication protein and thus indirectly cause lethality.
###end p 47
###begin title 48
Discussion
###end title 48
###begin p 49
###xml 48 52 48 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 144 148 144 148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 231 234 231 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA</italic>
###xml 297 305 297 305 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 336 344 336 344 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 580 584 580 584 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CTF4</italic>
###xml 781 783 781 783 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b069">69</xref>
###xml 784 786 784 786 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b075">75</xref>
###xml 1087 1089 1087 1089 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b076">76</xref>
###xml 1157 1164 1157 1164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1373 1375 1373 1375 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b076">76</xref>
###xml 1157 1164 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1242 1247 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
We find that 56 genes interact genetically with DNA2. Comparison of our results with those of previous synthetic lethal screens using 43 of the DNA2-interacting genes defines a set of pathways, all of which are interdependent with DNA2 and that form a network for preserving genome stability (see Figure 2). The six major hubs shown in Figure 2 link DNA replication, DNA repair, chromosome dynamics, checkpoints, chromosome structure/chromatin, osmotic stress, oxidative stress, and RNA metabolism. A major link to the cell cycle and the kinetochore occurs through a single gene, CTF4. Analysis of mutants that give rise to gross chromosomal rearrangements, the type of damage considered to be the most likely result of replication apparatus failure, identifies the same pathways [69-75]. The comprehensive nature of the SGA screen, however, allows greater insight into the structure of the network that coordinates these events. It is striking that this topology can be superimposed on the prokaryotic DNA replication interactome recently identified using protein-protein interactions [76]. The bacterial genome maintenance network consists of many of the E. coli orthologs (i.e., pol III holoenzyme, SSB, RecQ, RecG, SbcB, and RecJ) of the yeast replicative polymerase, its subunits, and the helicases and nucleases that form hubs and major nodes in our genetic network [76]. The common denominator in the diverse approaches was the use of a replication gene or protein as the bait. The parallels between the organisms point to evolutionary conservation in the coordination of processes that protect the genome. We suggest that the complexity of such processes was required for the evolution of large genomes, where the fidelity of the replication apparatus itself could not guarantee a sufficiently high level of accuracy and stability in genome transmission.
###end p 49
###begin p 50
###xml 131 142 131 142 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">discussions</xref>
###xml 147 149 147 149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b018">18</xref>
###xml 241 247 241 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MRE11,</italic>
###xml 380 384 380 384 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">XRS2</italic>
###xml 1050 1054 1050 1054 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
Current methods of scoring interactions do not result in identification, in the initial SGA screen, of every interacting gene (see discussions in [18]). To approach completeness, following identification of a single gene in a pathway, e.g., MRE11, in the SGA screen, we pursued "traditional" investigation, on a gene-by-gene basis, of other genes in the putative pathway, such as XRS2. Similarly, the identification of the Bre1p ubiquitylation pathway was interpreted only after testing downstream genes in the histone H2B modification pathway. This type of comprehensive genetic analysis is a powerful new tool for rapidly characterizing the full complement of processes requiring replication genes that might be coming under analysis for the first time, as well as rendering a coherent picture of years of genetic analysis of other genes. The genetic screen then enables one to rationally design experiments to determine, in molecular terms, the contribution of the replication protein to these processes. The outcome of such secondary analyses of DNA2 is discussed and interpreted below.
###end p 50
###begin title 51
###xml 72 116 72 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RNH32, RNH202, EXO1, YEN1, POL3, POL32, POL1</italic>
###xml 122 126 122 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PRI1</italic>
Stronger Links between Dna2p and OFP during Lagging-Strand Replication: RNH32, RNH202, EXO1, YEN1, POL3, POL32, POL1, and PRI1
###end title 51
###begin title 52
Structure-specific nucleases.
###end title 52
###begin p 53
###xml 46 50 46 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 55 60 55 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 132 136 128 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 279 283 275 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 288 292 284 288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rtf1</italic>
###xml 319 323 311 315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 328 332 320 324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">paf1</italic>
###xml 343 350 331 338 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s2">Results</xref>
###xml 608 612 596 600 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 666 687 654 675 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">(RNH32, RNH202, EXO1,</italic>
###xml 692 697 680 685 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YEN1)</italic>
###xml 856 858 844 846 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b014">14</xref>
###xml 961 966 949 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 972 977 956 961 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnh35</italic>
###xml 1022 1024 1002 1004 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b077">77</xref>
###xml 1130 1140 1110 1120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 rnh35</italic>
###xml 1150 1161 1126 1137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 rnh202</italic>
###xml 1419 1429 1391 1401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 rnh35</italic>
###xml 1573 1575 1541 1543 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b078">78</xref>
###xml 1578 1583 1546 1551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rnh35</italic>
###xml 1629 1631 1593 1595 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b079">79</xref>
###xml 1693 1702 1657 1666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 est1</italic>
###xml 1707 1718 1671 1682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 est2</italic>
###xml 1745 1747 1709 1711 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b017">17</xref>
###xml 1750 1762 1714 1726 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 rnh35</italic>
Although it has been known for some time that dna2 and rad27Delta are synthetically lethal, convincing genetic interactions between dna2 and other lagging-strand activities have not been previously identified. As shown by our demonstration in this work of synthetic lethality of dna2 and rtf1Delta and the viability of dna2 and paf1Delta (see Results), synthetic lethality with one gene in a pathway does not prove interaction with other genes in that pathway. Therefore, the identification of so many additional lagging-strand genes in the current study is a matter of some note. The synthetic lethality of dna2 with the genes encoding structure-specific nucleases (RNH32, RNH202, EXO1, and YEN1) provides the first evidence, to our knowledge, that RNA may be a substrate of Dna2p in vivo and strengthens evidence, as predicted from our in vitro studies [14], that Dna2p acts primarily if not exclusively on flaps in vivo. It has been known for some time that rad27Delta rnh35Delta is synthetically sick, but not lethal [77]. Since FEN1 is generally considered the major OFP nuclease, the more significant synthetic lethality of dna2 rnh35Delta and dna2 rnh202Delta was somewhat unexpected, and suggests that Dna2p also acts in an OFP pathway redundant with RNaseH2. Since Rnh35p does not act on flap-containing structures, the common substrate for RNaseH2 and Dna2p is probably RNA. Alternative to a role in OFP, the dna2 rnh35Delta synthetic lethality might reflect a redundant role for RNaseH2 and Dna2p in mRNA processing, an additional function proposed for RNaseH2 [78]. rnh35Delta mutants also have very short telomeres [79]. Since Dna2p is required for de novo telomere synthesis and dna2 est1 and dna2-2 est2 are synthetically lethal [17], dna2-1 rnh35Delta lethality could be related to events at telomeres.
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 15 19 15 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 23 27 23 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">EXO1</italic>
###xml 58 67 58 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 exo1</italic>
###xml 202 206 198 202 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">exo1</italic>
###xml 246 251 238 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mre11</italic>
###xml 383 385 371 373 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b042">42</xref>
###xml 517 519 505 507 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b027">27</xref>
###xml 555 564 543 552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 exo1</italic>
###xml 888 890 872 874 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b080">80</xref>
###xml 897 901 881 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yen1</italic>
###xml 907 913 887 893 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 970 974 950 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">YEN1</italic>
###xml 1005 1016 985 996 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen-0010061-sd001">Protocol S1</xref>
###xml 1076 1077 1056 1057 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">7</sup>
Suppression of dna2 by EXO1 overexpression, combined with dna2 exo1Delta synthetic lethality, suggests that Exo1p can provide a backup for Dna2p in OFP, with 5' flaps constituting the common substrate. exo1Delta is also synthetically lethal with mre11Delta, and it has been proposed that Exo1p participates in the resection of ends at DSBs in preparation for recombinational repair [42]. Exo1p may also be involved in a late step in the Msh2p-dependent mismatch repair pathway and perhaps in telomere end processing [27], which might also account for the dna2 exo1Delta lethality. There is no biochemical evidence as yet to show whether Yen1p is a structure-specific 5' to 3' nuclease, but this is likely given its similarity to FEN1 and Exo1p. Given that Yen1p is a preferential substrate of the Clb5p cyclin-dependent kinase required for proteins that function in G1 and early S phase [80], the yen1Delta dna2-2 synthetic interaction may reflect a direct link between YEN1 and DNA replication (see also Protocol S1). Since there are about 100,000 Okazaki fragments (1.5 x 107 bp per genome/100 bp per Okazaki fragment) during S phase, it is not surprising that multiple nucleases are involved in OFP.
###end p 54
###begin title 55
Pol delta.
###end title 55
###begin p 56
###xml 201 205 197 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 329 333 321 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 402 409 394 401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 530 532 518 520 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b081">81</xref>
###xml 550 557 538 545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 686 693 674 681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 699 703 687 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">msh2</italic>
###xml 713 717 697 701 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">exo1</italic>
###xml 813 825 793 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 852 858 832 838 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 949 961 929 941 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 971 972 951 952 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b008">8</xref>
###xml 1068 1075 1044 1051 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 1105 1110 1081 1086 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 1117 1119 1089 1091 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b081">81</xref>
###xml 1304 1306 1268 1270 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b033">33</xref>
###xml 1563 1565 1519 1521 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b033">33</xref>
###xml 1604 1616 1560 1572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 1724 1736 1680 1688 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol &#948;-DV</italic>
###xml 1795 1802 1743 1750 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27-d</italic>
###xml 1869 1874 1817 1822 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 1930 1953 1878 1901 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3 d-DV rad27-p rad51</italic>
###xml 1967 1969 1911 1913 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b011">11</xref>
Our genetic analysis supports the notion that Dna2p processes a specific subset of Okazaki fragment flaps-namely, those arising from excessive strand displacement by pol delta. We showed not only that dna2 is synthetically lethal with a mutant of pol delta that gives abnormally high levels of strand displacement, but also that dna2 is suppressed by a mutant that gives decreased strand displacement. pol3-01 is a mutation that inactivates the 3' to 5' exonuclease function of pol delta. This nuclease has three known functions [81]. First, because pol3-01 is a strong mutator, we can surmise that one function is in proofreading during DNA polymerization. Second, negative synergy of pol3-01 with msh2Delta and exo1Delta suggests a role in mismatch repair. These two activities are probably not relevant to the dna2 pol3-01 synthetic lethality since dna2-1 is not a mutator mutation and thus catastrophic mutagenesis is not likely to occur in the dna2 pol3-01 mutant ([8]; unpublished data). OFP is the third process proposed to require pol delta exonuclease, since pol3-01 is synthetically lethal with rad27Delta [81]. Mechanistically, this has been rationalized by the fact that pol delta 3' exonuclease is an inhibitor of the strand displacement activity of pol delta during in vitro DNA synthesis [33]. In the absence of its 3' exonuclease, pol delta can no longer idle at a nick, since the 3' displaced flaps that form as intermediates in idling cannot be removed nucleolytically. Instead, pol delta processively displaces the strand having a 5' terminus [33]. This is consistent with the idea of dna2 pol3-01 lethality stemming from the failure to efficiently process excessively long 5' flaps on Okazaki fragments. pol delta-DV is another exonuclease-deficient allele of pol delta, and rad27-d is a proliferating cell nuclease antigen noninteracting mutant of rad27. Overproduction of Dna2p suppresses the lethality of a pol3 d-DV rad27-p rad51Delta strain [11], supporting our conclusions.
###end p 56
###begin p 57
###xml 0 6 0 6 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 11 17 11 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 70 75 70 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">POL32</italic>
###xml 414 416 402 404 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b035">35</xref>
###xml 417 419 405 407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b043">43</xref>
###xml 512 517 496 501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 675 681 651 657 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 683 689 659 665 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol1&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 726 731 702 707 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 738 740 710 712 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b082">82</xref>
###xml 894 903 866 875 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">(pol32&#8211;8)</italic>
###xml 1029 1034 997 1002 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdc27</italic>
###xml 1034 1035 1002 1003 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1041 1066 1009 1034 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</italic>
###xml 1079 1085 1047 1053 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">POL32,</italic>
###xml 1111 1124 1079 1092 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe dna2</italic>
###xml 1126 1128 1094 1096 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b083">83</xref>
###xml 1172 1177 1140 1145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 1184 1188 1148 1152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ad27</italic>
###xml 1202 1204 1162 1164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b018">18</xref>
###xml 1212 1217 1172 1177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 1223 1227 1179 1183 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1253 1257 1209 1213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1275 1280 1231 1236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 1041 1066 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</span>
###xml 1111 1119 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
dna2-1 and dna2-2 mutants are suppressed by deleting the nonessential POL32-encoded subunit of pol delta that is required for optimum strand displacement. Pol32p is required for efficient in vitro DNA replication by pol delta in the presence of replication factor C, proliferating cell nuclease antigen, and a primed template. The ability to displace 5' ends is drastically decreased for pol delta lacking Pol32p [35,43], and the pol delta complex is expected to be defective in strand displacement synthesis in pol32Delta strains, thus reducing the need for Dna2p. Pol32p has also been shown to interact with pol alpha, and the same mutant that is synthetically lethal with dna2-2, pol1-1 (G493R), is synthetically sick with pol32Delta [82]. This might hint at coordination between Okazaki fragment initiation and elongation, although there is no reported phenotype associated with a mutation (pol32-8) that disrupts the Pol32p-pol alpha interaction. While this manuscript was being prepared, it was reported that a mutation in cdc27+, the Schizosaccharomyces pombe ortholog of POL32, suppresses one allele of S. pombe dna2 [83], so this suppression is conserved. Why is pol32Delta rad27Delta lethal [18] while pol32Delta dna2 grows more robustly than dna2 mutants? Loss of pol32Delta may shift the course of OFP from a flap removal pathway to one employing RNaseH. In the RNaseH pathway, FEN1 exonuclease may become essential to remove the last ribonucleotide, an activity that Dna2p does not appear to possess.
###end p 57
###begin title 58
Interaction with Pol alpha and Primase (and Mcm10p).
###end title 58
###begin p 59
###xml 59 63 59 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 69 75 69 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol1&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 85 93 85 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pri1-M4,</italic>
###xml 198 205 194 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pri1-m4</italic>
###xml 369 374 365 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2,</italic>
###xml 395 399 391 395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 491 495 487 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mec1</italic>
###xml 501 505 493 497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sml1</italic>
###xml 531 535 519 523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 571 578 559 566 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mcm10&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 580 582 568 570 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b023">23</xref>
###xml 595 600 583 588 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MCM10</italic>
###xml 718 720 698 700 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b084">84</xref>
###xml 721 723 701 703 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b085">85</xref>
###xml 758 762 738 742 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 767 772 747 752 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MCM10</italic>
###xml 883 890 863 870 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mcm10&#8211;1</italic>
Our demonstration here of synthetic lethal interactions of dna2 with pol1-1 and with pri1-M4, components of pol alpha-primase, may also fortify the argument that Dna2p participates in OFP. Although pri1-m4 has an S phase checkpoint defect in addition to a DNA replication defect, the replication defect is more likely to be responsible for the synthetic lethality with dna2, given our data that dna2 is not synthetically lethal with any of the mutations in major checkpoint genes, including mec1Delta sml1Delta. Certain alleles of dna2 are also synthetically lethal with mcm10-1 [23]. Recently, MCM10 has been implicated in elongation and in stabilizing pol alpha in vivo as well as in stimulating pol alpha in vitro [84,85]. The interdependent functions of DNA2 and MCM10 may reflect an interaction in lagging-strand replication. Alternatively, Dna2p might play a role in repair of mcm10-1-generated damage. The combined new data on interactions between Dna2p, pol Delta, pol alpha, and primase may be evidence for a previously unexpected coupling of primer synthesis, polymerase switching, and primer removal.
###end p 59
###begin title 60
###xml 48 52 48 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 66 71 66 71 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD27</italic>
Differences between the Genetic Interactions of DNA2 and Those of RAD27
###end title 60
###begin p 61
###xml 43 51 43 51 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 53 61 53 61 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen-0010061-st002">Table S2</xref>
###xml 130 135 130 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 158 160 154 156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b086">86</xref>
###xml 257 261 253 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 307 312 303 308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 466 471 458 463 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 478 480 466 468 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b069">69</xref>
###xml 481 483 469 471 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b087">87</xref>
###xml 494 499 482 487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2,</italic>
###xml 569 574 557 562 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 724 726 708 710 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b087">87</xref>
###xml 734 738 718 722 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 754 758 738 742 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 795 800 779 784 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 946 948 926 928 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b088">88</xref>
###xml 1069 1073 1049 1053 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 1097 1102 1077 1082 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD27</italic>
###xml 1366 1368 1338 1340 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b010">10</xref>
###xml 1369 1371 1341 1343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b033">33</xref>
###xml 1382 1386 1354 1358 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1420 1425 1392 1397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 1561 1563 1529 1531 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b016">16</xref>
###xml 1564 1566 1532 1534 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b087">87</xref>
###xml 1567 1569 1535 1537 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b089">89</xref>
###xml 1570 1572 1538 1540 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b091">91</xref>
###xml 1876 1880 1840 1844 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1890 1892 1854 1856 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b017">17</xref>
###xml 1893 1895 1857 1859 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b035">35</xref>
###xml 1896 1898 1860 1862 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b037">37</xref>
###xml 2123 2125 2087 2089 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b017">17</xref>
Comparison of the data presented here (see Figure 2; Table S2) and the results of a similar thoroughly validated SGA screen using rad27Delta as a query gene [86] reveals a wide (and unanticipated) divergence between genes that are synthetically lethal with dna2 and those that are synthetically lethal with rad27Delta. This divergence implies that the two enzymes may have slightly different sets of substrates. As pointed out in Results, the synthetic lethality of rad27Delta [69,87], but not dna2, with checkpoint mutants and with recombination mutants suggests that rad27Delta mutants probably accumulate more single-stranded DNA (the proposed signal for checkpoint activation) and more DSBs (repaired by recombination) [87], than dna2 mutants do. If dna2 mutants accumulate less damage than rad27Delta mutants, this in turn might suggest that FEN1 is the major OFP nuclease and that Dna2p is required at fewer (or different) sites than FEN1 [88]. This conclusion is consistent with other previously published evidence (despite the potential conundrum that deleting DNA2 is lethal and deleting RAD27 is not). First, pol delta, proliferating cell nuclease antigen, and FEN1 appear to act in a highly concerted fashion on templates that are optimal for pol delta efficiency in vitro, with little evidence that flaps longer than a few nucleotides are ever produced [10,33]. Second, dna2 mutants are weak mutators, while rad27Delta mutants are strong mutators, as measured by point mutations or stability of di- or trinucleotide repeats, or even larger repeats [16,87,89-91]. Dna2p may be specialized to function in OFP in genomic locations where the DNA sequence poses problems for pol delta, creating flaps that are not good substrates for FEN1. These regions are likely to include the rDNA and telomeres, since we have shown significant replication defects in these loci in dna2 mutants [17,35-37]. The role of Dna2p is not likely to be limited to these regions, however, as our previous immunofluorescence and chromatin immunoprecipitation analyses show Dna2p to be located at many other genomic regions during S phase [17]. Possible sites are replication slow zones or the inverted Ty repeats that give rise to genomic instability.
###end p 61
###begin p 62
If FEN1 is the major flap nuclease, either Dna2p might help FEN1 on some flaps or Dna2p might recognize discrete subsets of flaps and process them independently. The genetic differences observed, combined with the quantitative biochemical data that show that Dna2p is very inefficient at stimulating FEN1, even on long flaps, direct future attention to potentially independent roles for Dna2p and FEN1.
###end p 62
###begin title 63
The Helicase Network for Preserving Genomic Stability
###end title 63
###begin p 64
###xml 70 74 70 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sgs1</italic>
###xml 84 88 80 84 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">srs2</italic>
###xml 186 188 178 180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b092">92</xref>
###xml 455 457 447 449 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b093">93</xref>
###xml 580 584 572 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 719 728 711 720 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g001">Figures 1</xref>
###xml 733 734 725 726 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g002">2</xref>
###xml 764 771 756 763 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t002">Table 2</xref>
Previous screening of the nonessential gene knock-out collection with sgs1Delta and srs2Delta as queries identified a so-called helicase network defined by a set of common interactions [92]. Genes in this network are implicated by dozens of recent studies in the repair of damaged replication forks through sister chromatid recombination and replication restart mechanisms, but coupling of the network to DNA replication remains poorly understood (e.g., [93]). By reversing the screening process and using an essential lagging-strand replication gene as query, we have found that dna2 is synthetically lethal with mutations in all of these helicases and in the genes with which they interact. The interactions shown in Figures 1 and 2 and our subsequent work (see Table 2) suggest that Dna2p may be one of the major replication proteins that coordinate this helicase network and replication.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 27 38 27 38 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 sgs1</italic>
###xml 75 80 71 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad51</italic>
###xml 87 94 79 86 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 390 396 382 388 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 434 436 426 428 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b094">94</xref>
###xml 437 439 429 431 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b095">95</xref>
###xml 496 501 488 493 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SGS1,</italic>
###xml 628 633 620 625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD51</italic>
###xml 667 678 659 670 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 sgs1</italic>
###xml 721 725 709 713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SGS1</italic>
###xml 798 802 786 790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 961 963 949 951 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b096">96</xref>
###xml 1129 1131 1117 1119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b097">97</xref>
###xml 1149 1153 1137 1141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 1255 1259 1243 1247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1289 1293 1277 1281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">srs2</italic>
###xml 1361 1366 1345 1350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RAD51</italic>
###xml 1368 1373 1352 1357 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SRS2,</italic>
###xml 1435 1437 1419 1421 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b098">98</xref>
###xml 1438 1441 1422 1425 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b100">100</xref>
###xml 1462 1473 1446 1457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 sgs1</italic>
###xml 283 288 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 427 432 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 490 495 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
The synthetic lethality of dna2-2 sgs1Delta and its lack of suppression by rad51Delta (Table 2) suggests that Sgs1p participates directly in DNA replication by aiding Dna2p in stimulating flap cleavage during OFP under some circumstances. This interpretation is attractive since the human Sgs1p orthologs, BLM and WRN, interact physically with Dna2p and suppress the replication defects in dna2-1 mutants when overexpressed in yeast [94,95]. (The suppression could not be investigated with yeast SGS1, since its overproduction is toxic [A. Morgan, personal communication; unpublished data].) The reproducible effect of deleting RAD51 in restoring defective growth to dna2-2 sgs1Delta mutants, however, is consistent with SGS1 playing an additional role in a late stage of recombinational repair of dna2-induced lesions, such as in the resolution of Holliday junction intermediates into viable products, a reaction that requires Sgs1p in conjunction with Top3p [96]. Dna2p might be required to remove 5' ends of nascent DNA in reversed forks, while Sgs1p serves as a helicase to resolve the forks, like RecJ and RecQ in bacteria [97]. Lesions due to DNA2 deficiency do have the potential to lead to lethal recombination intermediates, because we find that dna2 is synthetically lethal with srs2Delta and that this lethality is efficiently suppressed by deleting RAD51. SRS2, given its role in inhibiting an early step in recombination [98-100], probably prevents dna2-2 sgs1Delta-derived lesions from entering the recombinational repair pathway. Thus, the interaction between Sgs1p and Dna2p is multipotential.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 179 182 179 182 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b101">101</xref>
###xml 183 186 183 186 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b104">104</xref>
###xml 346 351 346 351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad51</italic>
###xml 382 393 382 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rrm3</italic>
###xml 430 434 426 430 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3</italic>
###xml 533 544 525 536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rrm3</italic>
###xml 606 610 594 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3</italic>
###xml 616 620 600 604 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">srs2</italic>
###xml 630 634 610 614 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3</italic>
###xml 640 644 616 620 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sgs1</italic>
###xml 693 695 665 667 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b047">47</xref>
###xml 696 698 668 670 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b075">75</xref>
###xml 763 772 735 744 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 rrm3</italic>
