###xml 845 849 813 817 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3</italic>
###xml 855 859 819 823 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sgs1</italic>
###xml 922 927 882 887 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 933 937 889 893 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3</italic>
###xml 972 974 924 926 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b047">47</xref>
###xml 991 995 943 947 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1000 1004 952 956 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3</italic>
###xml 1058 1062 1006 1010 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fob1</italic>
###xml 1110 1121 1054 1065 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 rrm3</italic>
###xml 1135 1142 1075 1082 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t002">Table 2</xref>
###xml 1353 1355 1293 1295 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b012">12</xref>
###xml 1356 1359 1296 1299 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b105">105</xref>
Rrm3p promotes DNA replication through non-nucleosomal protein-DNA complexes, including the rDNA RFB, Rap1p-binding sites in the telomere, inactive ARS sites, and centromere DNA [101-104]. Rrm3p may act on the same replication intermediates as Dna2p rather than on downstream toxic intermediates formed during repair of faulty replication, since rad51 mutations do not suppress the dna2-2 rrm3Delta synthetic lethality. Recently, rrm3Delta has been tested for synthetic lethality against a number of candidate gene deletions. Unlike dna2-2 rrm3Delta, most of the synthetically lethal combinations, such as rrm3Delta srs2Delta and rrm3Delta sgs1Delta, were suppressed by recombination mutants [47,75]. Thus, early replication intermediates cause cell lethality in dna2 rrm3Delta mutants, while recombination intermediates cause cell lethality in rrm3Delta sgs1Delta mutants. These intermediates may not involve FEN1, since rad27Delta rrm3Delta is not synthetically lethal [47]. Although both dna2 and rrm3Delta mutants show significant pausing in the rDNA, a fob1Delta mutation did not restore viability to the dna2-2 rrm3Delta mutant (Table 2), so there are additional sequences replicated by these genes. We have recently demonstrated that Dna2p can stimulate FEN1 cleavage of long flaps with secondary structure, but that the reaction is inefficient [12,105]. Since Rrm3p is a 5' to 3' helicase, Rrm3p is a candidate for a helicase that may aid Dna2p in flap processing.
###end p 66
###begin title 67
DNA Repair
###end title 67
###begin p 68
###xml 24 28 24 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 133 137 133 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 165 167 165 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b016">16</xref>
###xml 395 399 395 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 409 410 409 410 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b008">8</xref>
It does not appear that dna2 interacts with genes involved in nucleotide excision repair, consistent with the relative resistance of dna2 mutants to UV irradiation [16]. Base excision repair (long patch) involves all of the proteins also involved in OFP, and therefore a role for Dna2p in base excision repair would be supported by the interactions found in this work and the MMS sensitivity of dna2 mutants [8]. A role for Dna2p in an unidentified Rad52p-dependent pathway was discussed above.
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 27 31 27 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 243 247 243 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 253 261 253 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 464 467 464 467 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b106">106</xref>
###xml 554 557 554 557 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b106">106</xref>
###xml 1037 1041 1037 1041 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1364 1365 1364 1365 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b007">7</xref>
###xml 1422 1432 1422 1432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2 mre11</italic>
###xml 1456 1460 1452 1456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 1516 1524 1512 1520 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 1526 1528 1522 1524 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b048">48</xref>
###xml 1529 1532 1525 1528 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b107">107</xref>
###xml 1645 1651 1641 1647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1656 1664 1652 1660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad50&#8211;5,</italic>
###xml 1700 1705 1696 1701 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad52</italic>
###xml 1516 1524 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
The synthetic lethality of dna2 with each member of the Mre11p complex may contribute to emerging evidence that the Mre11p complex functions at the replication fork. First, the seven genes whose interactions overlapped most significantly with dna2 (see Figure 2) are also synthetically lethal with the genes of the Mre11p complex. Second, the Mre11p complex associates with chromatin primarily during S phase, and this association does not appear to require DSBs [106]. It has been suggested that the Mre11p complex assists sister chromatid association [106], and that this association is required for recombinational repair of DSBs during DNA replication. Another view derives from the fact that the Mre11p complex and Exo1p are both required for activation of the Rad53p checkpoint kinase after inhibition of replication by HU. This leads to the inference that the Mre11p complex and Exo1p may convert DSBs arising at stalled replication forks into single-stranded DNA, a signal for subsequent repair. Since replication forks stall in dna2 mutants, the synthetic lethality with mutations in Mre11p complex components or Exo1p could be explained by a failure to produce the single-stranded DNA signal. It is possible that DSBs that arise during normal DNA replication are repaired in Mre11p complex mutants, but are lethal in cells lacking both Mre11p and Dna2p [7]. Finally, or alternatively, the synthetic lethality of dna2 mre11Delta may indicate that DNA2 is involved in a telomere defect, as has been shown in S. pombe [48,107]. We cannot eliminate the possibility that the Dna2p/Mre11p interaction is involved in repair, but we note that dna2-2 and rad50-5, which is as deficient in repair as rad52Delta, are epistatic with respect to repair.
###end p 69
###begin title 70
Sister Chromatid Cohesion
###end title 70
###begin p 71
###xml 21 25 21 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 83 85 83 85 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b017">17</xref>
###xml 86 88 86 88 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b035">35</xref>
###xml 89 91 89 91 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b037">37</xref>
###xml 131 135 131 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">FOB1</italic>
###xml 174 185 174 185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 ctf4</italic>
###xml 359 363 355 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 410 421 406 417 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2 ctf4</italic>
###xml 427 431 419 423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fob1</italic>
###xml 745 748 733 736 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b108">108</xref>
###xml 895 898 883 886 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b109">109</xref>
###xml 945 951 933 939 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1161 1165 1149 1153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 1306 1308 1294 1296 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b035">35</xref>
###xml 1309 1311 1297 1299 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b037">37</xref>
Replication forks in dna2 mutants pause at the RFB in the rDNA, where DSBs result [17,35,37]. Our current finding that deletion of FOB1 suppresses the synthetic lethality of dna2-2 ctf4Delta damage could be explained if Ctf4p-mediated sister chromatid cohesion is necessary to repair damage at the RFB due to defective Dna2p. This requirement for cohesion in DNA2 mutants is not limited to the rDNA, since the dna2-2 ctf4Delta fob1Delta strain is ts and radiation sensitive. Thus, the Dna2p deficiency must give rise to damage requiring cohesion for repair elsewhere in the chromosome as well. A role for cohesion in maintaining the replication fork during stalling or collapse is attractive since cohesion is required for efficient DSB repair [108]; a role for sister chromatid cohesion in preventing excessive sister chromatid exchange due to breaks at the RFB has been directly demonstrated [109]. We note that our analysis of replication in dna2-2 strains by two-dimensional gel electrophoresis indicates a high incidence of stalled replication forks at sequences throughout the rDNA, not limited to the RFB, suggesting general replication fork stalling in dna2 mutants and providing physical evidence of a more delocalized requirement for sister chromatid cohesion, perhaps throughout the chromosome [35,37].
###end p 71
###begin title 72
Chromatin Remodeling, Disassembly, and Reassembly
###end title 72
###begin p 73
###xml 521 525 521 525 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 530 536 530 536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol1&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 711 713 707 709 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b056">56</xref>
###xml 720 726 716 722 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol1&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 887 893 879 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol1&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1017 1019 1005 1007 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b056">56</xref>
###xml 1236 1238 1220 1222 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b052">52</xref>
###xml 1239 1241 1223 1225 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b054">54</xref>
###xml 1242 1245 1226 1229 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b110">110</xref>
###xml 1302 1305 1286 1289 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b111">111</xref>
###xml 1455 1458 1435 1438 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b112">112</xref>
###xml 1459 1462 1439 1442 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b113">113</xref>
###xml 1563 1567 1543 1547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 1161 1166 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 1426 1431 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
During DNA replication, the chromatin in front of the replication fork is disassembled and then reassembled behind the fork. Our new findings add to recent findings from many sources that are providing the first insight into the molecular links between the replication machinery and chromatin dynamics. Dna2p interacts with both Asf1p and yFACT. The Asf1p/Dna2p interaction in chromatin assembly/remodeling is too ill-defined for further inferences at the moment. However, the allele-specific synthetic lethality between dna2 and pol1-1 suggests that Dna2p participates in the recently demonstrated interplay between Spt16p (a component of the FACT-like nucleosome reorganization factor), Ctf4p, and pol alpha [56]. The pol1-1 mutant protein fails to interact with Spt16p and shows altered temporal interaction with Ctf4p. The compromised association between Spt16p and pol alpha in the pol1-1 mutant is accompanied by a delay both in pol alpha recruitment to late origins and its release, leading to a slow S phase [56]. By adding a link between Dna2p and this particular aspect of pol alpha function, our results support the model of the Formosa lab that the yeast Spt16p complex is likely to be directly involved in DNA replication [52-54,110], as has also been suggested for the frog FACT complex [111]. The Spt16p remodeling complex may facilitate the movement of pol alpha and Dna2p through nucleosomes, as proposed for human FACT in transcription [112,113]. The caveat that yFACT defects might result in reduced transcription of gene(s) that interact with DNA2 was mentioned above.
###end p 73
###begin p 74
###xml 6 10 6 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 202 206 202 206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 211 215 211 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad6</italic>
###xml 408 411 408 411 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b114">114</xref>
###xml 414 418 414 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">set1</italic>
###xml 493 497 493 497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">set1</italic>
###xml 732 736 732 736 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 738 741 738 741 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b114">114</xref>
###xml 742 745 742 745 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b115">115</xref>
Other DNA2-interacting genes encode specific sets of histone modification enzymes that catalyze histone ubiquitylation, methylation, and deacetylation. We discovered here that the synthetic sickness of dna2 and rad6 is related to Rad6p/Bre1p-mediated ubiquitylation of histone H2B, which in turn leads to methylation of H3 at the lysine at position 4 by the SET1 complex, containing Set1p, Swd1p, and Swd3p [114]. set1 mutants are sensitive to HU and may accumulate DNA damage during S phase. set1 was not recovered in the SGA screen because it is not in the deletion collection. Ubiquitylation and methylation alter silencing and chromatin structure at the rDNA and at telomeres, which may suggest a mechanism for interaction with dna2 [114,115].
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 161 166 161 166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rad27</italic>
###xml 173 178 169 174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
###xml 190 193 182 185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gs1</italic>
###xml 236 240 224 228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hst3</italic>
###xml 247 249 231 233 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b018">18</xref>
###xml 250 253 234 237 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b116">116</xref>
###xml 256 260 240 244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HST3</italic>
###xml 314 323 298 307 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hst3 hst4</italic>
###xml 519 522 503 506 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b117">117</xref>
###xml 525 529 509 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 595 599 579 583 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RPD3</italic>
###xml 771 773 755 757 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b067">67</xref>
###xml 774 776 758 760 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b068">68</xref>
###xml 800 804 784 788 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hst1</italic>
###xml 811 815 791 795 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hst3</italic>
###xml 822 826 798 802 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rpd3</italic>
###xml 833 837 805 809 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bre1</italic>
###xml 844 849 812 817 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spt16</italic>
###xml 856 860 820 824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cac2</italic>
###xml 871 876 831 836 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">vid21</italic>
###xml 921 929 877 885 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pgen-0010061-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1036 1047 992 1003 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen-0010061-sd001">Protocol S1</xref>
The interaction between Dna2p and Hst3p and the Rpd3p/Pho23p histone deacetylases is interesting because mutations in ORC, the replication initiator, as well as rad27Delta, pol32Delta, and sgs1Delta also show synthetic interaction with hst3Delta [18,116]. HST3 performs a redundant function in DNA replication but hst3 hst4 cells have phenotypes indicative of replication defects, such as increased rates of chromosome loss and mitotic recombination, decreased telomere silencing, and hypersensitivity to UV treatment [117]. DNA2 is the only DNA replication gene thus far found to interact with RPD3. Histone deacetylation by the Rpd3p/Pho23p complex has been previously implicated in the temporal regulation of origin activation, but not elongation, in DNA replication [67,68]. The observation that hst1Delta, hst3Delta, rpd3Delta, bre1Delta, spt16Delta, cac2Delta, and vid21Delta are all linked to the network shown in Figure 2 suggests that the existing nucleosome structure has been optimized for high fidelity DNA replication (see Protocol S1).
###end p 75
###begin title 76
Conclusions
###end title 76
###begin p 77
###xml 543 545 543 545 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b094">94</xref>
###xml 590 594 590 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 599 604 599 604 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RFA1,</italic>
###xml 743 745 743 745 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b013">13</xref>
###xml 746 749 746 749 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b118">118</xref>
###xml 1086 1088 1070 1072 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b015">15</xref>
###xml 1244 1246 1228 1230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b076">76</xref>
###xml 391 396 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1461 1466 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
We propose that the genome maintenance network is coordinated by physical interaction of the replication proteins with the complexes that carry out regulation and repair. A good deal of evidence supports this. Originally we found that Dna2p co-purified with FEN1 and later demonstrated the genetic interaction. We discovered a genetic interaction between Dna2p and BLM and WRN helicases-the human orthologs of Sgs1p-and then found that this genetic interaction also represented a direct physical interaction between Dna2p and those helicases [94]. Others found genetic interactions between DNA2 and RFA1, encoding the single-stranded DNA binding protein RPA, and similarly documented a physical interaction between the proteins Dna2p and RPA [13,118]. Indeed, most DNA replication proteins multitask and are components of many complexes. Pol delta and epsilon are involved in DNA repair complexes as well as replication complexes. Pol epsilon is, in addition, involved in the S phase checkpoint. FEN1 itself is involved in multiple reactions, including long patch base excision repair [15]. Though circumstantial, the resemblance between the basic topology of the genetic network described here and the proteomic network described in bacteria [76] further suggests the model that replication proteins physically coordinate repair and regulatory genome maintenance complexes. We anticipate that this model will be verified in detail when proteomic approaches in yeast yield the kind of comprehensive data that can already be obtained from genetic screens such as SGA.
###end p 77
###begin title 78

###end title 78
###begin title 79

###end title 79

###xml 440 444 368 372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">can1</italic>
###xml 449 465 373 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">::MFA1pr-HIS3-Mf</italic>
###xml 470 483 390 403 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1pr-LEU2 his3</italic>
###xml 488 494 404 410 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1 leu2</italic>
###xml 499 506 411 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0 met15</italic>
###xml 511 517 419 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0 ura3</italic>
###xml 522 524 426 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0;</italic>
###xml 544 557 448 461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1::URA3;</italic>
###xml 577 590 481 494 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2::URA3;</italic>
###xml 603 663 507 567 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MATa ade2&#8211;1 can1&#8211;100 his3&#8211;11,15 leu2&#8211;3,112, trp1&#8211;1 ura3 RAD5</italic>
###xml 713 715 617 619 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b019">19</xref>
All strains used in the study are found in Table S4. The strains used in the SGA screen and subsequent verification were as follows: 4741 MATa his3Delta1 leu2Delta0 met15Delta0 ura30Delta; 4741 Mat alpha his3Delta1 leu2Delta0 met15Delta0 ura3Delta0; strain 4741dna2-1-6D (MB100) MATa dna2-1his3Delta1 leu2Delta0 met15Delta0 ura3Delta0; strain 4741dna2-2-11D (MB101) MATalpha dna2-2::LEU2 his3Delta1 leu2Delta0 met15Delta0 ura3Delta0; Y3656 can1Delta::MFA1pr-HIS3-Mfalpha1pr-LEU2 his3Delta1 leu2Delta0 met15Delta0 ura3Delta0; Y3656dna2-1; Y3656 dna2-1::URA3; Y3656dna2-2; Y3556 dna2-2::URA3; and W30W303 MATa ade2-1 can1-100 his3-11,15 leu2-3,112, trp1-1 ura3 RAD5. Y3656 is derived from strain 4741 as described [19]. Unless otherwise noted, all haploid deletion mutants used in this work were in strain 4741 and all double mutants were tested using 4741dna2-1 or Y3656dna2-2 as indicated.
###end p 80
###begin title 81
SGA screen.
###end title 81
###begin p 82
###xml 54 56 54 56 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b019">19</xref>
###xml 188 192 188 192 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 327 330 327 330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b119">119</xref>
###xml 431 437 431 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 455 461 455 461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 734 740 734 740 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 787 793 781 787 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
The SGA screen was performed as previously described [19]. Y3656dna2-1 and Y356dna2-2 were constructed for this study and used as query strains. SGA analysis was performed for each of the dna2 alleles. Genes that showed synthetic lethality or synthetic sickness in the primary screen were tested by standard tetrad dissection [119]. For the secondary tetrad analysis, new heterozygous diploids were constructed between MB100 (4741 dna2-1) and MB101 (4741 dna2-2) and each of the candidate deletion mutants in strain 4741 (Invitrogen, Carlsbad, California, United States). Thus, each synthetic interaction that is reported here was tested using two independent diploids, one in the original screen and one in the secondary screen. The dna2-2 dissections were incubated at 30 degreesC and dna2-1 dissections at 23 degreesC. Any strain failing to generate viable double mutants was deemed synthetically lethal. A strain was considered synthetically sick if tetrads gave fewer double mutants than expected and double mutants grew slower than either single mutant. At least ten tetrads were dissected for each double mutant, and usually more were dissected.
###end p 82
###begin title 83
X-ray and MMS sensitivity.
###end title 83
###begin p 84
###xml 173 175 173 175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b016">16</xref>
###xml 243 248 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
The X-ray source was Pantak (East Haven, Connecticut, United States) MK II 70 kev 20 ma. The source was calibrated and experiments were carried out as previously described [16]. For the MMS sensitivity assay, 0.005% and 0.01% MMS was added to yeast-peptone-dextrose (YPD) plates after autoclaving, and plates were used the same day.
###end p 84

###begin title 236
Clustering Analysis
###end title 236
###begin p 237
###xml 68 72 68 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 134 138 134 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2</italic>
###xml 144 151 144 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 589 594 589 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2,</italic>
###xml 603 608 603 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol32</italic>
Hierarchical two-dimensional clustering analysis was applied to the DNA2 interactions and those of 43 genes synthetically lethal with DNA2 (see Table 1). The interactions were clustered with respect to the results of the current screen and 43 previous screens using these genes as queries. A total of 322 genes and 876 interactions, each indicated by a red box, were identified. This panel shows a zoom into the region of most significant overlap of shared genetic interactions. In addition to including reduced fitness genes, this analysis includes genes that give increased fitness with dna2, such as pol32Delta.
###end p 237
###begin title 238
A Genome Stability Network
###end title 238
###begin p 239
###xml 52 56 52 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 75 82 75 82 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pgen-0010061-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 124 126 124 126 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b018">18</xref>
###xml 127 129 127 129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b019">19</xref>
###xml 130 132 130 132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b092">92</xref>
###xml 206 210 206 210 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrm3</italic>
###xml 217 219 213 215 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b047">47</xref>
###xml 220 222 216 218 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b075">75</xref>
###xml 267 275 263 271 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pgen-0010061-st002">Table S2</xref>
Data were compiled with the Payek program using the dna2 screen results in Table 1 and the results of the previous screens [18,19,92], as well as data compiled for candidate genes synthetically lethal with rrm3Delta [47,75]. The data are presented in tabular form in Table S2.
###end p 239
###begin title 240
###xml 15 19 15 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
Suppression of dna2 by ExoIp Overexpression
###end title 240
###begin p 241
###xml 12 18 12 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 143 149 143 149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GAL110</italic>
###xml 191 209 191 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 7A(pRS424G)</italic>
###xml 214 234 214 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1(pRS424G-EXO1)</italic>
###xml 287 292 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Strain W303 dna2-1 was transformed with the plasmids pRS424G and pRS424G-EXO1, an empty plasmid vector and a plasmid expressing ExoIp from the GAL110 promoter, respectively. W303RAD5 strains dna2-1 7A(pRS424G) and dna2-1(pRS424G-EXO1) were grown to mid log phase and serially diluted on yeast-dextrose galactose- and raffinose-containing plates and incubated at 30 degreesC for 5 d.
###end p 241
###begin title 242
###xml 28 32 28 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>
###xml 37 44 37 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3&#8211;01</italic>
Synthetic Lethality Between dna2 and pol3-01
###end title 242
###begin p 243
###xml 12 18 12 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 30 44 30 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TRP1 CEN3 DNA2</italic>
###xml 89 101 89 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3 pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 111 114 111 114 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b120">120</xref>
###xml 197 201 197 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">POL3</italic>
###xml 236 243 236 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 287 294 287 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 450 459 450 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2 TRP1</italic>
###xml 480 483 480 483 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pgen-0010061-b121">121</xref>
###xml 492 506 492 506 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 632 646 632 646 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2&#8211;1 pol3&#8211;01</italic>
###xml 666 674 666 674 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DNA2 TRP</italic>
Strain W303 dna2-1 carrying a TRP1 CEN3 DNA2 plasmid was transformed with an integrating URA3 pol3-01 plasmid [120] cut with BamH1. The transformants were streaked on 5-FOA medium to excise the WT POL3 gene and identify clones with the pol3-01 mutation. Three transformants carrying the pol3-01 mutation (isolates 2, 8, and 11) were restreaked on YPD medium containing 2-amino-5-fluorobenzoic acid (FAA), which selects for strains that have lost the DNA2 TRP1-containing plasmid [121]. Three dna2-1 pol3-01 colonies showing some residual growth on the FAA plates were restreaked on YPD-containing medium. The same three isolates of dna2-1 pol3-01 but containing the DNA2 TRP plasmid, i.e., that had not been grown in the presence of FAA, are shown as controls, as indicated.
###end p 243

###xml 50 54 50 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dna2</italic>

###begin p 247
###xml 6 13 6 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">, pol32</italic>

###end p 247

The following spores were recovered: 11 WT, 21 dna2-2, 26 fob1Delta, 17 ctf4Delta, 18 dna2-2 fob1Delta, 20 ctf4Delta fob1Delta, zero ctf4Delta dna2-2, and six dna2-2 ctf4Delta fob1Delta. Since the triple mutant grew slowly at 30 degreesC, another 27 spores were dissected and incubated at 23 degreesC. The following spores were recovered: 14 WT, nine fob1Delta, 14 ctf4Delta, seven dna2-2, 14 dna2-2 fob1Delta, nine ctf4Delta fob1Delta, zero dna2-2 ctf4Delta, and nine dna2-2 ctf4Delta fob1Delta.
